Important Report by Chiang Kai-shek at the National Government Memorial Week 36

The Original Text, Sorted, Was Released Yesterday as a Supplement

(Nanjing) Central News Agency: Chairman Chiang delivered an important report at the National Government Memorial Week on the 2nd. The original transcript was not released because it was awaiting sorting and review. However, the foreign newspapers in Shanghai recently published excerpts, which omitted many important points and often distorted the original meaning. The full text is as follows:

Fellow comrades, I have a few things to explain regarding the recent discussions between the representatives of the Central Government and Guangdong in Shanghai, which I will report on now. Yesterday, Shanghai newspapers published news saying they would thoroughly investigate the two telegrams issued by the Central News Agency regarding the reform proposal of the Guangdong party and government, and the Central Government's response. One telegram was sent by Tiecheng, instructed by the representatives sent to Shanghai by the Central Government. The other was the Central Government's reply, regarding the party and government reform proposal, which I signed and issued. Both original telegrams are on file. Yesterday's Shanghai newspapers mentioned investigating the source. Now, I can read these two original telegrams to you. The telegram from Shanghai arrived on October 28th. The original text is as follows: "Respectfully to Chairman Chiang, Secret: Before this morning's meeting, the Guangdong representatives proposed a party and government reform plan. Mr. Cai [Yuanpei] and others believe that this plan is of great importance, and the Central Government has not been informed in advance, making it inconvenient to discuss. The plan is hereby telegraphed for your consideration. (Note: The original text of the plan can be found in this newspaper on the 31st). Mr. Cai and others request instructions on how to respond. Please instruct us to follow." Tiecheng. Our telegram in response reads: "To Mayor Zhang of Shanghai, Secret, translated and forwarded to Mr. Li and Mr. Tiecheng. Tie brothers, I have read the telegram. Without discussing the content of the party and government reform proposal, its spirit is inconsistent with the call for unity against external aggression. At this time, for the sake of the party and the nation, the only option is to quickly gather in the capital and face the national crisis together. Fundamental issues of party and government should await the discussion and resolution of the majority of the party. There is no reason why a dozen people can decide on the overall plan for the entire party and nation by negotiating in the concessions. Since we are party members, we must abide by the party constitution together. As citizens, we should respond to the nation's crisis. If we are truly loyal comrades, loving the party and saving the country, and acting out of sincerity, rather than seeking to divide spoils as outsiders criticize, then such proposals that violate the party constitution and disregard the national crisis should not be proposed for discussion, so as not to betray the people's fervent hopes. This is our reply, Chiang Kai-shek." From the original text of this telegram, the truth of the matter is clear. There is no need for much explanation. Currently, the Central Government is extremely willing to unite sincerely and face external aggression together. All these trivial details have not been taken into account. They can publish and post whatever they want, and we have ignored it. However, yesterday's record seemed to say that the Central Government fabricated the telegram, and it was never released, so we have to prove the facts. The news published in Shanghai newspapers is almost entirely from the Guangdong side. The Central Government has remained silent throughout, hoping for the success of unity. We hope the National Kuomintang can understand this. However, there should be a clear understanding of what is published in the newspapers. Now that the nation is in crisis, there should be a judgment of right and wrong. We advocate respecting freedom of speech, but it is absolutely not permissible to overturn right and wrong and obliterate facts in the name of freedom of speech, causing public confusion and social unrest. Under such circumstances, the unity of the party will not only fail to help the party and external affairs, but will also increase the difficulties of diplomacy and push the country further into danger. As a result, the foundations of the country and the hearts of the people will be completely shaken. Is this the way to unite sincerely? If the representatives from Guangdong to Shanghai are uniting sincerely, with the sincerity to face the national crisis together, they would never disregard the shaking of people's hearts and the foundations of the country. As for the Central Government comrades, as long as this unity can be achieved as soon as possible, they can endure any grievances and pains. Therefore, we regard everything that has happened in the past as the past, and only seek to unite and fight against external aggression. However, when the Central Government seeks unity too eagerly, some people may think that the Central Government is in trouble, and everything must be subject to their control. It is as if the current Central Government has been conquered, and everything must accept the orders of Guangdong. Moreover, the Guangdong government has not conquered the Central Government. Even if it conquered the Central Government, what glory is there? Not to mention the Central Government, even if I, Chiang Kai-shek, personally succumb to the Guangdong comrades, is it not just party members succumbing to party members, senior friends succumbing to juniors, Chinese people succumbing to Chinese people? What victory or glory is there to speak of? Or perhaps some people think that the existence of the Guangdong government can restrain the Central Government, and shake the Central Government's diplomatic position. In principle, if the Guangdong representatives truly want to unite and fight against external aggression, for the sake of diplomacy, the Guangdong government should quickly and unconditionally abolish itself, in order to achieve national unity. It should not retain the form of the Guangdong government confronting the Central Government, otherwise it would be helping the Japanese to bully our country, which is not the true principle of uniting to save the country and the party. This is the first point that should be explained to everyone. Secondly, for the sake of eagerly hoping for unity, although we do not have to strictly talk about right and wrong, we should have a very honest attitude towards friends or enemies according to the principles of being human. We hope that friends will all be good people, and that even enemies can eventually become friends. Only with Dr. Sun Yat-sen's spirit of universal love can one be considered a follower of Dr. Sun Yat-sen. Therefore, we should not let our friends, or even our enemies, do things that damage their character. The principles we rely on for revolution are: first, Dr. Sun Yat-sen's doctrine and all his last instructions; second, the party constitution of our party; and third, the Provisional Constitution. If a friend comes to advise us that the party constitution can be compromised to comply with the wishes of a few people, this is something we cannot do. If someone says that the Provisional Constitution, although it represents the will of the people of the whole country, does not need to be observed, and we only need to comply with the words of a few Guangdong comrades, then this is also something we cannot do, as it would obliterate the public opinion of the people of the whole country, violate the Provisional Constitution established by the people of the whole country, and the party constitution established by all party members, listen to the instructions of a few people, and sacrifice the overall interests of the entire people and all party members. Since we are friends, why should we tell our friends to violate the public opinion of the people? A gentleman loves others with virtue. The reason why the affairs of the Chinese nation are not going well is mostly because of accommodating personal feelings and disregarding the great difficulties of the party and the country. In particular, when right and wrong are unclear, we must pay extra attention. Now that the nation is in crisis, we rely entirely on the guidance of the party's predecessors to lead us on a bright and righteous path. It is absolutely not good to force people to do things that violate the party and the country and sacrifice the public opinion of the entire country, or to use the opinions of a few people and local issues to shake the whole country, so that the central government has no way to handle diplomacy. I think the old comrades in Guangdong love the party and the country, and would never do such a thing. Someone may slander me, and I, Chiang Kai-shek, personally can endure it, but I absolutely cannot violate the laws and regulations of the party and the country, let down our people, or betray Dr. Sun Yat-sen. I have already made up my mind that even if all the people of the country and all the comrades are willing to violate the Provisional Constitution and the party constitution, I, Chiang Kai-shek, personally cannot destroy the Provisional Constitution or violate the party constitution. I hope that the senior comrades in Guangdong will take the attitude of revolutionary predecessors to guide us younger generations, so that we younger generations will not do things that betray the party and the country, violate the law and disrupt discipline, and create disasters for the next few decades. I have already told the Guangdong representatives in Shanghai that they are all predecessors, and I am a junior. If the predecessors teach us with good examples, then there is nothing we will not follow. If a bad seed is left today, I fear that it will forever be the sinner of the party and the country in the future. Therefore, as long as all the predecessors come up with a bright and upright attitude and method, all of us party members will definitely be willing to follow and walk on the bright and upright road. There will be no reason to oppose. I believe that no predecessor can call on us to violate the party constitution and destroy the Provisional Constitution. We cannot repeat the disastrous mistakes of the past twenty years. That kind of disaster has not stopped by the twentieth year of the Republic of China. Are we still willing to create another twenty years of disaster in the future? I think the old comrades should make our party members have a sense of respect, and not make our younger generations betray the party and violate the law, let alone make our younger generations lose respect and courtesy. If the younger generations are disrespectful and impolite to the predecessors, although the blame lies with the younger generations, the predecessor old comrades are also responsible. We very much hope that all the comrades in Shanghai have a deep understanding of this. Now is the time of national crisis. It is absolutely not effective for a few people to discuss day after day in Shanghai, and no major national plan can be discussed in the concessions, leaving the capital aside. When the Song ministers' discussions were not settled, the Jin soldiers had already crossed the river. If things come to this, the country will not exist, so what is the point of personal matters? At this time, as long as it is beneficial to the party and the country, everything about individuals is not a problem. Therefore, I gave them the telegram expressing my willingness to step down on the day the Guangdong comrades arrived in Shanghai, and I have already signed it and asked them to release it. However, they did not advocate releasing it at the time, but today they seem to think that I have broken my word, which is a pity. In fact, the draft prepared by Guangdong unilaterally for me without my consent was disclosed unofficially by the Guangdong side in newspapers in Guangzhou and Hong Kong in early October, so that newspapers in Tianjin and Beiping reprinted them one after another, causing unrest among the people of the whole country, thinking that I was about to resign and step down, causing complete unease among the society, the army, and the general public. The Guangdong comrades first disclosed their own draft, which was drafted by themselves but without my consent, everywhere, and on the other hand, the original draft signed and submitted by me on the day they arrived in Shanghai, said that it was not yet time to release it and put it aside, only making the people of the country panic and shake, and guessing about my departure and stay. If they truly love the party and the country, love the younger generations, and unite sincerely, I believe they would not intentionally play with us younger generations. Later, the Guangdong representatives sent another letter, saying that the intention of this telegram was not to abandon responsibility. This clearly wants me to continue to bear heavy responsibilities even on the verge of leaving, but after this telegram is sent, how can this responsibility be shouldered? It only makes the Chinese and foreign psychology unclear about where the central authority is entrusted, and no one is responsible for internal and external affairs, and the danger of the country is even more unspeakable. Therefore, I wrote to Mr. Cai and Mr. Zhang on the 30th of last month, saying that today the people are panicking and the dangers are even clearer. It is inappropriate to simply issue a telegram expressing our position. We must first appoint a legally responsible successor before issuing this telegram, and the day the telegram is issued should be the day I actually resign and relinquish responsibility. We must not leave any gaps to interrupt the country's politics. In this autumn of crisis and survival, we people have a heavy responsibility to the party and the country, and we must not deceive people and play games with national affairs, causing the country to fall into a state of anarchy. Therefore, I said that I can sacrifice anything personally, but I cannot destroy the country's laws and regulations, destroy the foundation of the government, or destroy the system of our party handed down by Dr. Sun Yat-sen. Recently, someone mentioned that a comrade in Shanghai said that not only should Chiang step down, but also Chiang should go abroad and never be allowed to return to China. Some people even said that this was said by Mr. Hu [Shih]. I really don't believe it, because Mr. Hu has always been teaching us to love and protect us, and he has no prejudice. If I am wrong, he can clearly blame me, why say this? Even if he said this, it is just a casual joke, not something he really wants to say from the bottom of his heart. Therefore, I do not ask whether anyone said this. As for my personal position, as long as it is beneficial to the party and the country, I am willing to be expelled, even to die. If my resignation can make the party and the country healthier and diplomacy can be victorious, I am willing to die. If I did not have this determination to die, I would not be in Nanjing today. If I did not have the determination to sacrifice myself for the party, I would have been chased away by the conspiracy of the Communist Party, who sold short, bought empty, and fabricated rumors to slander me in the fifteenth and sixteenth years of the Republic of China. If I did not have the determination to sacrifice myself for the country in the face of danger, I could have been chased away by the Japanese artillery fire in Jinan in the fifteenth year. The methods of the Communist Party and the Japanese warlords are like this, but we comrades should always be close and sincere. Even if we do not show concern for friends and relieve their difficulties, we should leave some room for the sake of the country and the history of Dr. Sun Yat-sen. Friends can only see sincerity in times of crisis, and revolution must also respect our duties and abide by the laws and regulations of the party and the country more and more in times of increasing crisis in order to be considered revolutionaries. Foreign friendly countries view the future of our China entirely on whether our central government and government comrades can fight to the end, and not be shaken by the changes in a part of Guangdong and the disputes of a few people in Guangdong, undermining the credibility of our central government in the international community. Perhaps the friendly countries know that when our central government is in this kind of internal and external attack, it can still fight to the end, be responsible and unremitting, and be worthy of being a friend in the international community, and will pay more attention to the Chinese character and help us complete the revolutionary cause. Therefore, it is absolutely impossible to use a few local issues to restrain diplomacy, shake the country, and obliterate Dr. Sun Yat-sen's life, the party system, and the historical facts of the revolution. Therefore, I believe that the senior comrades in Guangdong would never have such intentions, and I believe that they will eventually love the party and the country, realize peace, come to the capital together, and face the national crisis together, and never let this unity break down again. I originally proposed three principles at the beginning of the contact with Guangdong, and I still abide by these three principles: First, if the Guangdong side can take full responsibility, then the comrades in the Central Government can make all concessions. Please move the comrades in Guangdong as a whole to the capital and reorganize the government. As for Chiang Kai-shek personally stepping down, there is no problem. As long as the Guangdong side can reliably take responsibility and come to take over, then Chiang Kai-shek can issue a telegram to step down. Second, if the Guangdong side cannot take responsibility, then it should be presided over by the Central Government, and the Guangdong government should be abolished. The Guangdong comrades should gather in the capital together to face the national crisis together. Third, if cooperation is desired from all parties, then Chiang Kai-shek welcomes it even more, but we must come to Beijing to discuss in person, which is the way to be open and honest and share the same boat. What we are taking now is the third path, but just sitting in Shanghai and discussing the party and government reform system without coming to the country's difficulties only makes the night long and dreamy, and makes people panic. Not only can it not reduce the central government's difficulties, but it also makes the party and the country more

Page 8

Ministry of Foreign Affairs Officially Announces the Tao Peng Case Has Been Resolved 37

The Company Commander Huang Who Shot Tao Peng

Has Been Sentenced to Fourteen Years of Imprisonment

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs officially announced on the 4th that the Tao Peng case has been resolved. The Tao Peng case, which caused a sensation in June of this year, has now been found to have been shot by Company Commander Huang Zhenwu, stationed in Suzhou. As a result of the military law trial, Huang has been sentenced to fourteen years of imprisonment. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs' note to the British ambassador and the summary of the investigation are recorded as follows:

The Ministry of Foreign Affairs' note to the British Ambassador to China on October 20 states: Regarding the Tao Peng missing case, the Acting Minister recalls that in June, British consular officials conducted investigations in Kunshan and Suzhou based on rumors about the case. The results of the investigation and attachments have been sent to the Ministry. According to the attachments, it appears that Tao Peng was involved in a shooting incident near Kunshan on the night of June 1. On the morning of the 2nd, he was captured by military police and taken to Suzhou on the same day. In early July, representatives from the Ministry of Military Affairs and the Ministry conducted investigations and did not obtain the same results as the British consular officials. On July 29, Your Excellency the Ambassador was instructed to present a note from Your Excellency's government to the President of our country, which the President immediately ordered Vice Minister Chen Ci of the Ministry of Military Affairs to investigate thoroughly. The Ministry also slightly mentioned the investigation on August 6. Vice Minister initially found it difficult to start the investigation due to a lack of direct evidence, so he had to be cautious, which prevented his work from ending as early as the government had hoped. By September 25, his investigation had yielded considerable results, and former Minister Wang had requested verification of the details of Tao Peng's causing trouble and being arrested, as well as the person in charge of the custody. The Acting Minister has now approved the detailed report sent by the Vice Minister to the Ministry. According to the report, it can be seen that the British government's concerns about Tao Peng's fate are indeed well-founded. After Tao Peng shot and killed two military policemen, he was arrested in Kunshan on June 2 and killed by Company Commander Huang Zhenwu in Suzhou on the 8th. The Chinese government cannot but inform Your Excellency the Ambassador of this and express deep regret. Moreover, Company Commander Huang wanted to conceal the truth of this case, even from the government itself, but now it is clear from the report, so the Chinese government cannot but express regret again. Recalling that the shooting incident near Kunshan occurred when the wind of agitation in the country was at its peak, and at that time, all the military police on the Jinghu Railway had been ordered to pay close attention to suspicious persons. Tao Peng was arrested and taken to Suzhou after the shooting incident, just under this circumstance. Moreover, Tao Peng's violent behavior and the strange objects found in his belongings, as well as his refusal to reveal his name and nationality, could not but arouse suspicion that he intended to engage in activities that endangered national security. However, due to this kind of fear and the inability to recognize who Tao Peng was at that time, he could not be handed over to British officials after his capture. Company Commander Huang has now been sentenced to fourteen years of imprisonment as a result of the military law trial, as stated in the report. The Chinese government has also circulated the verdict to all military officers to inform them. This is what the Acting Minister wishes to mention. As for the assistance of British officials in providing evidence to help clarify the incident, the Chinese government expresses its gratitude. In short, the Acting Minister wishes to reaffirm the Chinese government's determination to uphold the meaning of modern law and implement it in China, and the Chinese government hopes that the British government can believe that it is sincere in implementing this principle in the measures taken in this case. Accordingly, a copy of the original report is sent to Your Excellency the Ambassador for your information. It is necessary to inform you that this note is addressed to His Majesty's Ambassador to China, Sir Miles Lampson.

Summary of the Tao Peng Case Report: On the evening of June 1 of this year, three military policemen were patrolling the Jinghu Railway when they saw a suspicious person walking hurriedly on the railway tracks. They immediately issued a password to order him to stop, but he did not listen. So they went forward to check and found that he was a foreigner. Unexpectedly, the foreigner immediately opened fire and shot two military policemen to the ground. At that time, an express train passed by, and the foreigner escaped, leaving behind a bag containing a pistol, a handful of bullets, a small knife, a small bottle of chloroform, a paper mask, and other items. The foreigner was arrested the next day and taken to Suzhou. Company Commander Huang interrogated him, but the foreigner refused to tell him who he was. He only said that he came from Shanghai, had no passport, admitted that the bag belonged to him, and refused to tell the reason for shooting the military policemen. Company Commander Huang believed that the foreigner's behavior was suspicious and that he must be a foreign bandit, intending to send him to the court, but he planned to wait for the injured military policemen to recover and obtain their evidence before transferring him. On June 7, Company Commander Huang learned that one of the military policemen who had been shot had died from his injuries, and the other was also difficult to save (he also died later). So on the 8th, he interrogated the foreigner again. During the interrogation, the company commander was filled with righteous indignation, and the foreigner suddenly took advantage of the company commander's unpreparedness and pounced on him. The company commander drew his pistol and shot him, killing him. Company Commander Huang knew that his behavior was excessive, so he destroyed all the evidence along with the body and ordered all the soldiers not to leak the information. Therefore, the first investigation did not yield any results. Later, his subordinates revealed the truth, and Company Commander Huang was taken into custody and sent to the military law trial. It was found that the foreigner shot by Company Commander Huang was indeed the Englishman Tao Peng. As a result of the trial, he was sentenced to fourteen years of imprisonment. (Special dispatch on the 4th)

Zhang Zongchang Arrives in Tianjin 38

(Tianjin) A reporter took a train to Tanggu at 5:30 in the morning on the 4th. At 7:20, the Tencho Maru docked, and Zhang Zongchang was already standing on the deck. The reporter boarded the ship to interview him, exchanging a few words, and then went to the special train prepared on the Beining Road to talk in detail. Zhang's boldness and generosity were no less than in the past. He said, "The Japanese army's occupation of Liaoning and Jilin is extremely distressing. All citizens are indignant. People are trying to use me to harm the eastern provinces. How can I be fooled by them? However, there are many Japanese who came to surround me. I once told them that I am an outsider who does not ask about national affairs. I have no opinion on the Northeast Incident and will not express any opinion." The Japanese had no way to deal with me. However, I have long wanted to leave Dalian to avoid being used by the Japanese as a tool for spreading rumors. Although the Japanese cannot openly prevent me from acting, they also do not want me to leave. Recently, Deputy Commander Zhang sent a representative to invite me to Beiping. I then decided to leave Dalian to explain the misunderstanding. I am now a citizen, and it is inconvenient to express opinions on national affairs lightly, but the north has suffered such a heavy blow, and our citizens cannot ignore it and should think of a way. Some time ago, everyone hoped that the League of Nations would uphold justice and make fair sanctions. Now it seems like a mirage. In my personal opinion, the governing officials should not mention any grudges, abandon the idea of rights, cooperate fully, and adopt the opinions of the people. The whole country should be united, and then diplomacy will have strength and negotiations will have success. I hope that at this time of national survival, everyone will argue about opinions, fight for rights, and fail to cooperate with external affairs, then what will the future be like? I dare not say. I will stay in Tianjin for a day or two and then go to Beiping." Then he asked the reporter about the peace conference situation and was extremely concerned. Speaking of this, Zhang Liang's representative Wang Zhen, Zhang Xueming's representative Tao Weiduo, Gao Jiyi's representative Fu Qiang, Pan Fu's representative Yang Bin, Sun Dianying's representative Li Delu, and Lin Xianzhu, Jin Shouliang, Wang Dong, Ma Dunyuan, Gu Zhen, Liu Ziqing, Guo Zhen, Teng Jie, San Du Shang, Qiu Suzhen, Liang Jiheng, Li Baoshu, Liu Zhenbang, Shi Liuhua, Wang Shenzhi, Hao Mengjiu, Yin Shaochang, Wu Jiyu, Zhang Shaojiang, Gao Yiting, Han Yisan, Cheng Boke, Zhang Shiguang, Qian Mingyu, Zhou Zhicheng and other thirty people, took a special train from Tianjin and arrived in the morning to visit. At 8:30, he left Tanggu and arrived in Tianjin at 10:20. Zhang Xueming, Xu Wenguo, Wang Yimin, Dong Shien and other twenty people welcomed him at the East Station. After Zhang got out of the car and exchanged greetings, he was accompanied by Li Shiku and others to Jin Shouliang's residence to rest. (Special dispatch on the 4th)

Important Foreign Telegrams

Candidate for British New Cabinet's Chancellor of the Exchequer Undecided 63

Baldwin Declines to Serve as Chancellor of the Exchequer

Austen Declares Unwillingness to Join the Cabinet

New Parliament Holds Its First Meeting the Other Day

Party Members Appoint New Leaders

Reuters, London, 3rd - Who will fill the position of Chancellor of the Exchequer in the new cabinet? This is the question on everyone's lips. Prime Minister MacDonald has now gone to the birthplace of Lord Lothian for a short rest and will return on Sunday. It is generally thought that the formation of the cabinet is proving more difficult than initially anticipated. However, it is not unexpected that the list of cabinet members will be announced before the Prime Minister's return. The most closely watched position is that of Chancellor of the Exchequer. Conservative Party members of Parliament generally believe that Neville Chamberlain is best suited to manage finances, but MacDonald seems unwilling to appoint someone with such strong views on tariffs as Chamberlain to this position. Therefore, some Conservative Party members are gradually becoming resentful. MacDonald, considering Baldwin's more moderate views on tariffs, invited Baldwin to serve as Chancellor of the Exchequer, but Baldwin declined. Once the candidate for Chancellor of the Exchequer is announced, the tariff policies that MacDonald's new government intends to implement will be known. Austen Chamberlain, who previously served as Foreign Secretary in Baldwin's Conservative government and as First Lord of the Admiralty in the pre-election National Government, is now 68 years old. He has written to Conservative Party leader Baldwin, stating that he is unwilling to accept a cabinet position. At noon today, the new Parliament held its first meeting and elected FitzRoy as Speaker. Today, members of the National Liberal Party held a meeting and unanimously decided to appoint the renowned legal scholar Sir John Simon, the former leader of the Indian Constitutional Reform Commission, as their leader. Labour Party members also met today and unanimously elected Lansbury as the leader of the Labour Party members of Parliament. Lansbury is 71 years old and previously served as Minister of Works in the Labour cabinet. Labour Party members still trust Henderson and have asked him to remain as party leader. Although Henderson was defeated in this election, his parliamentary career will not be interrupted as he will eventually secure a seat.

Reuters, London, 4th - In British city elections, the Conservative Party has won almost everywhere. The Conservative Party has captured 338 seats from the Labour Party, and the Labour Party has lost a total of 416 seats.

Laval and French, German Ambassadors Discuss Debt Issues 64

Reuters, Paris, 3rd - French Prime Minister Laval today discussed with the German Ambassador to France the progress of his negotiations in Washington and France's attitude towards international debt, lasting two hours. French Finance Minister Flandin was also present. The German Ambassador will report the content of the discussions to the German government, and Laval will be notified of the German government's attitude shortly.

National News, Berlin, 4th - After the first conversation between German Ambassador to France Hoesch and French Prime Minister Laval, Hoesch sent a long coded telegram late last night to report his impressions and opinions to the German government. To prevent leaks, he avoided using long-distance telephone. This morning, the German government held a special cabinet meeting to discuss the matter, the content of which remains strictly confidential.

National News, Paris, 4th - Paris newspapers commenting on the talks between the French Prime Minister and the German Ambassador show a distinct optimism. Le Matin stated that, according to official reports, the meeting focused on returning to the Young Plan. It also stated that Flandin frankly expressed France's hope that Germany would make at least some payments on the debt after the end of the Hoover Moratorium. It also stated that the two sides discussed inviting the International Committee of Bankers to reconsider Germany's ability to pay in accordance with the Young Plan.

Amidst the Ceasefire on Armaments, the United States Advocates a Major Naval Plan 65

National News, Washington, 3rd - Today, the idea of a major naval plan has resurfaced in the US capital. Bradon, Chairman of the House Naval Appropriations Committee, announced that after the new Congress convenes next month, he will propose an appropriation of $120 million US dollars for naval construction. This bill only provides funding for the first year of a new shipbuilding program, which aims to bring the strength of the US Navy equal to that of the British Navy. According to Bradon's plan, it is proposed to use $120 million to build one 10,000-ton cruiser equipped with six-inch guns and aircraft, one small aircraft carrier, fifteen destroyers, and five submarines.

Soviet Russia Experiences a Severe Fuel Shortage 66

National News Agency, Moscow, 3rd - Fuel is becoming increasingly scarce within Russia. In order to regulate the situation, the authorities have issued orders to manage the waste of fuel. The use of coal and charcoal is subject to strict control. According to the new regulations, all fuel is only allowed for cooking needs. All other public and private buildings are only allowed to light fires once a day. The Moscow authorities recently announced that all public and private buildings should light fires once every other day, but now they have limited it to once every three days, indicating that the shortage of coal in Soviet Russia is increasing daily.

Important News

Zhang HaiPeng Invades Heilongjiang Again 72

Zhang Recruits Bandits to Attack the Provincial Capital in Two Routes

Japanese Army Advances Toward the Tao'an-Ang'angxi Railway Under the Pretext of Repairing a Bridge

Harbin Correspondence: The battles along the Tao'an-Ang'angxi railway line could have come to an end after Zhang HaiPeng's troops were routed. However, Zhang HaiPeng was unwilling to accept defeat after retreating to Tao'an, and deliberately intended to disturb Heilongjiang again. However, his troops were scattered and his strength was insufficient. Therefore, he tried his best to recruit bandits to replenish his forces. Even the workers of the Tao'an-Ang'angxi railway, who were captured during the retreat, were forcibly drafted into the army. He has now claimed to have one cavalry brigade and two infantry brigades. Zhang and his son, Zhiming, each command an infantry brigade. The cavalry brigade was expanded and reorganized from the original Second Regiment and is commanded by Jing Guofen, the former regimental commander. Guns and ammunition are supplied by the Japanese. On October 24, the Japanese army transported military supplies in four train cars from the Siping-Tao'an Railway to Tao'an, which were received by Zhang's troops. The Japanese also provided Zhang with 100,000 Japanese yen for military expenses to be used to recruit and pacify bandits. Currently, bandits in the seven counties and four banners within the Mongolian border are flocking to Zhang because of his wealth and promise of official positions. Zhang is recruiting both large and small bandit groups. As of now, he has recruited more than 2,700 bandits. However, while Zhang is recruiting bandits to expand his strength, he is also sending telegrams to Zhang Xueliang, Zhang Zuoxiang, Wan Fulin, and others in Beiping, expressing remorse and falsely claiming that his previous entry into Heilongjiang with his troops was an unavoidable matter. He will close his doors to reflect on his mistakes, reside in Liaoning, hand over his troops to his son, Zhiming, and allow the Heilongjiang army to reorganize them. At the same time, Zhang also telegraphed Ma Zhanshan of Heilongjiang, saying that he would close his doors to reflect on his mistakes. The Heilongjiang provincial authorities thought that Zhang had sincerely repented and sent Wu Songshan's brigade to send officials to verify the reorganization of Zhang's troops nearby. However, before Wu's brigade could dispatch officials, Zhang suddenly sent someone to say that the roster of officers and soldiers had not yet been completed and requested that the verification be postponed. Ma Zhanshan was quite surprised by his evasion and sent Wang Jingxiu, the chief of staff of the National Defense Preparatory Office, to Tao'an to secretly investigate the movements of Zhang's troops. Wang returned to the province on the 28th and reported that Zhang HaiPeng was indeed still harboring ulterior motives and would invade Heilongjiang again. His plan is to launch the attack when the Nenjiang River freezes, so that he can cross the river on the ice without the need for boats. He will attack the capital of Heilongjiang in two routes. One route, led by Zhang and his son, Zhiming, will advance with two infantry brigades along the Tao'an-Ang'angxi railway line. The other route will be a separate detachment, led by cavalry brigade commander Jing Guofen, which will secretly cross the river towards Zhaodong and attack the flank of the provincial capital, and also use it to divide the Heilongjiang army's forces. After receiving the report, Ma Zhanshan actively made arrangements, ordering Su Bingwen, the commander of the Second Infantry Brigade, to temporarily remain in the provincial capital to assist in military affairs, and mobilized Su Bingwen's and Zhang Dianjiu's brigades to defend the Dongping area and block the defense of Zhaodong. He also sent a letter to Ding Chao, the commander of the Eastern Railway Protection Army, requesting him to assist with the defense. Ding ordered the 174th Regiment of the 26th Brigade, stationed at the Yimianpo station on the Harbin-Suifenhe line, to deploy two armored trains to the Ang'angxi-Mangou station section of the Harbin-Manzhouli line yesterday. If necessary, the entire 26th Brigade will be transferred to strengthen the force. It is observed that if this military operation is launched, the scope of the disturbance will be broad, and the battle will not be as easy to end as before. The Japanese are determined to help Zhang attack Heilongjiang, acting unilaterally. First, the Chinese Eastern Railway's Dumien Timber Company will provide White Russian firearms to disrupt the Eastern Railway line, which will divert the Heilongjiang army's forces. There are reports that the White Russian leader, Semenov, secretly arrived in Harbin a few days ago, and his old troops have mostly been ordered to concentrate at Boketu. The White Russians who recently invaded the Boketu forest area are those White Russians, who are said to have about 600 firearms. Heilongjiang must telegraph Cheng Zhiyuan's brigade in Manzhouli and send troops to suppress them quickly. Second, the Japanese army will directly attack Heilongjiang. On the 25th of this month, two Japanese military officers went to Heilongjiang to meet Ma Zhanshan, saying that they were under the orders of their commander, Honjo, to ask Ma to hand over the government and peacefully cede it to Zhang HaiPeng. Ma refused, and the two military officers left in a huff. On the same day, Shimizu, the Japanese consul in Heilongjiang, suddenly sent a note to the provincial government, stating that the Tao'an-Ang'angxi railway was built with loans from the South Manchuria Railway (SMR), and the current interruption of traffic is detrimental to the interests of the SMR. The SMR will send workers to repair the Jiangqiao bridge. The provincial government immediately replied, stating that only two of the Jiangqiao bridges on the Tao'an-Ang'angxi railway were destroyed, and the damage was minor. The railway bureau has been ordered to repair them as soon as possible. China's railways have sovereignty, and Chinese workers can repair them as well, so there is no need for others to interfere. After the reply, on the afternoon of the 28th, the Japanese consul suddenly sent a final ultimatum with strong language, stating in substance: "The Tao'an-Ang'angxi railway is a railway built with loans from the South Manchuria Railway and is of great importance to transportation and the economy. If it is allowed to remain in its current state, it is absolutely impossible for the Chinese side to repair the bridge on its own. Therefore, the South Manchuria Railway, which has a close relationship, has decided to send people to begin the repair work. It is hoped that the Jiang province army will not interfere and will provide appropriate protection. If the repair work is interfered with, the Japanese side will take appropriate measures." On the same night, the Japanese Second Division, together with the South Manchuria Railway's garrison, totaling about 1,000 troops, arrived in Tao'an by troop train and notified the railway bureau to inform the Heilongjiang province to order the troops stationed on the Tao'an-Ang'angxi line to temporarily withdraw from the railway line. The Heilongjiang authorities believe that this move by the Japanese army is intended to cover up Zhang HaiPeng's invasion of Heilongjiang and, in addition to telegraphing Beiping, are ordering the troops on the Tao'an-Ang'angxi railway to temporarily retreat when the Japanese army advances. Therefore, it is expected that Zhang HaiPeng's troops will attack Heilongjiang during the day. (October 30)

Japanese Troops Collude with Bandits to Invade Tongliao a Second Time 73

The Ordeal of Tongliao Refugees in the First Invasion

A dispatch from Beijing reports that since the first day of the month, Japanese troops, using aircraft and armored vehicles to shield Mongol bandits, have again bombarded the north and south railway stations of Tongliao (the North Station is a station on the Zheng-Bai branch of the Si-Tao Railway, and the South Station is a station on the Da-Tong branch of the Bei-Ning Railway) and the city with artillery and machine guns. A telegram has already been sent reporting this, making it clear that Japan is disregarding the League of Nations and expanding its military operations as much as possible. It is unknown what their ultimate aim is. This ordeal of Tongliao is now the second time it has occurred. On the 15th of last month, the Japanese troops carried out a major destruction there. However, due to inconvenient transportation and obstructed communication, the Beijing side only knew that Japanese aircraft had dropped many bombs there on that day, killing fourteen people, while the detailed situation was largely unknown to the outside world. Now, according to the accounts of those who fled Tongliao to escape the disaster, the course of this battle is worth recording, so it is specially recorded below: "Tongliao is close to Inner Mongolia. In places such as Da-Hao-Zi and Da-Lin stations, there have been large numbers of Mongol bandits gathering since the beginning. After the Japanese troops occupied Liaoning and Jilin, they considered Tongliao to be in a strategic location, connected to Si-Tao in the north, which could reach Heilongjiang, and bordering Bei-Ning in the south, which could directly reach the Shanhaiguan Pass. Furthermore, Rehe was to its southwest. If they did not take control of it early and cut off the connection between Heilongjiang and Rehe, their military operations would be affected. Therefore, they sent messengers to extensively instigate the Mongol bandits, promising to supply them with weapons and money to launch an attack on Tongliao. The Mongol bandit leader Bao Bao-chen and others were incited and recruited Mongol people, providing them with weapons and plotting a planned and organized attack, calling it the 'Zhonghe National Inner Mongolia Independence Army.' Their flag was blue with a red sun. On October 13th, a Japanese armored vehicle suddenly arrived at Tongliao North Station, carrying Japanese man named Hayata and Bao Bao-chen, among others. After getting off the vehicle, they went to the Chamber of Commerce to visit Magistrate Wang and others, saying that they were acting on the orders of the Japanese military commander to order the county to quickly plan for independence and to send people to Da-Lin Station to welcome the Mongol soldiers and jointly establish an independent government. Magistrate Wang sternly refused. The Japanese left in frustration. That evening, the Mongol bandits split into two groups and launched an attack. The northern route was the Mongol bandit cavalry, advancing along the county seat. The southern route was the Japanese armored vehicle, protecting the Mongol bandits' advance along the railway line. The Northeast Army's 40th Regiment was originally stationed in the city, but because they had been ordered not to resist, they retreated en masse to Tuo-Zi, an area about three miles south of the railway line. At dawn on the 14th, more than 500 Mongol bandits stormed the city. Seeing that the city gate was not closed and the garrison had withdrawn, they rushed into the city, burning civilian houses and shelling shops. Tianqing Company was the first to be hit. The fire illuminated the sky, and the sounds of killing shook the earth. The people wailed in pain, leading their children and supporting their wives. The scene was too horrible to witness. At this time, there were still police groups in the city who were motivated by righteous indignation to open fire and resist. Local gentry Zhang Zhong-ge and Wang Zhen-duo also led the merchant and civilian groups to resist to the death in the streets, resulting in extremely fierce street fighting. The 40th Regiment outside the city heard the gunfire in the city and rushed to help. The Mongol bandits' weapons were supplied by the Japanese and were very sophisticated, and there were Japanese officers directing them. As a result, Zhao En-shun, the commander of the 1st Company, was killed in action, and the situation was on the verge of collapse. Fortunately, Regiment Commander Wang Qi-feng and Police Chief Yang Xi-bin fought to the death. After about five hours of stalemate, more than 200 Mongol bandits were killed. Seeing that they could not hold out, they began to collapse and retreat. There was an old man named Zhang (his first name is unknown), who was originally a cart driver at Tongliao Station, but then abandoned that profession to become a bandit. He gathered more than 600 people, but because he lacked military supplies, his momentum was still small. The Japanese troops detected this and sent people to instigate him, urging him to disturb the Tao-Liao area, giving him 600 Mauser rifles, 600 sets of military uniforms, 200 rounds of ammunition per person, and 20 silver dollars, scheduling a date for him to attack. On the 14th, when the Mongol bandits had already been defeated, the Japanese troops recruited Zhang to start an uprising. On the morning of the 15th, several Japanese aircraft were covering the bandits who were about to advance. Unexpectedly, Zhang still had blood and spirit and refused to obey the Japanese command, turning against them. Although the Japanese aircraft dropped bombs at the station to cover the advance of the newly transferred Mongol soldiers, Zhang intercepted and attacked them from behind, and attacked them from the front and back with the garrison and police groups in the city. One Japanese aircraft was shot down, and many Mongol bandits were killed. More than 40 Japanese personnel were directing the attack, and a few were also injured or killed. The Japanese military's plan failed, and they gnashed their teeth at Zhang. On the 16th, a Japanese steel armored vehicle carrying 60 Japanese soldiers arrived in Tongliao, intending to retaliate. Upon hearing the news, Zhang dug dozens of deep pits, about four feet wide, on the railway tracks west of Tongliao.

Page 10

The pits were covered with straw, and soil was spread over the straw, and the railway tracks were reinstalled. He led his troops to ambush in the nearby high sorghum fields. When the Japanese steel armored vehicle passed by, the front railcar passed safely. When the steel armored vehicle arrived, there was a loud crash, and it fell into the pit. Zhang then led his troops to rush out and loot the weapons from the vehicle, killing many Japanese soldiers. In the afternoon, the Japanese military sent a crane to lift the steel armored vehicle out and pursued Zhang. But Zhang had already led his troops far away, and the Japanese military could do nothing. This was the course of the first Japanese collusion with Mongol bandits to invade Tongliao. Now that they have come again, their desire for revenge is even greater. It is feared that the incident will escalate, and the city of Tongliao will suffer even more from the Japanese troops' ravages." (November 2nd)

Japanese Spread Rumors in Tianjin 74

So-called Information Bureau Releases Statement by Italian Consul

Italian Acting Consul Sends Letter to North China Star to Correct

A dispatch from Tianjin reports that since the Northeast Incident occurred, the Japanese in Tianjin secretly organized a so-called Information Bureau, which publishes all kinds of strange and absurd rumors in English every day that are unfavorable to China, and distributes them to consulates and foreign organizations to confuse the foreigners in Tianjin. The English newspaper "North China Star" in Tianjin did not make a judgment and published a statement by the Italian Consul in Shenyang released by the bureau on the 30th. After seeing the newspaper, the Italian Acting Consul immediately sent a letter to correct it, and stated that the Italian Consul had never issued any statement. This shows the ugly state of the Japanese spreading rumors. The news report and the Italian Acting Consul's correction letter are translated as follows:

On the 30th of last month, the English newspaper "North China Star" in Tianjin published a telegram from the Japanese Information Bureau in Shenyang on the 29th, saying that the Italian Consul in Tianjin had recently traveled to Shenyang and made the following statement to a British reporter stationed in Shenyang: "It is almost impossible to demand that the Japanese troops withdraw to their original positions. It is not appropriate to withdraw troops until peace and order are restored in the northeastern provinces of China. In my personal opinion, the current situation will continue for a considerable period of time, but in the end, China and Japan can hope to reach a compromise. I also believe that similar autonomous governments will inevitably appear in certain parts of China, independent from Nanjing and other Manchurian provinces. Discussing the restoration of the Qing Dynasty in the current environment is almost completely useless." The Italian Acting Consul Jia Fu-te wrote a letter saying: "Dear reporter, today's newspaper published a piece of news with the headline 'Italian Consul General Says Withdrawal of Troops is Almost Impossible.' I am ordered to write to your newspaper to correct it. The Italian Consul stationed in Tianjin recently went to Shenyang due to special events, and did not meet with reporters, nor did he issue any statement to anyone. Please publish this letter in your newspaper. Thank you. Italian Acting Consul Jia Fu-te, October 31, 1931, in Tianjin."

Inspection Notes from Shenyang 75

A dispatch from Shenyang reports that since the Japanese military forcibly occupied Shenyang, they have arbitrarily destroyed everything in our country. Regarding military deployments, Japan is actively expanding. I recently went to Shenyang again to investigate and saw the tragic situation in the city. I am truly filled with a sense of the past and present. I will record in detail what I heard and saw in Shenyang to inform those who care about Shenyang.

The section of the Bei-Ning Railway from Ju-Liu-He to Huang-Gu-Tun has long been under the violent control of the Japanese military. All passengers traveling to and from must undergo strict inspections and interrogations. Once the eastbound train passes Xin-Min Station, all passengers are uneasy, their faces filled with worry, and they say to each other, "We are about to pass the mountain of knives, we must be careful." Everyone rummages through their suitcases and boxes, checking themselves, and throwing any business cards or envelopes with titles out the window, because if they are found by the Japanese military, their lives will be in danger. When the train arrives at Ju-Liu-He, four or five Japanese military policemen, accompanied by one Chinese and one Japanese ruffian, board the train to inspect and search. Those with small courage see the fierce appearance of the ruffians and reveal a little bit of panic. If they are unfortunately seen by them, they will be ordered to take off their clothes for inspection, regardless of gender, and they will be endlessly questioned about their whereabouts. I personally saw six passengers on the same train being detained and taken off the train, one of whom was a female who looked like a student because she had a picture of her deceased father in military uniform, and the servant who accompanied me, named Shi Yao-cai, was also among them. In this serious environment, I could only watch them being dragged off the train, unable to help, but my heart was filled with anger, as if it were being fried in oil. After a day and a night, Shi was fortunately released. According to him, he was detained in the Tian-Tai Inn in Huang-Gu-Tun, and the Japanese soldiers pointed guns at him from time to time, forcing him to report on the deployment of our army along the Yu-Guan and Jin-Xian lines, treating him like a spy. Fortunately, he benefited from the calluses on his palms and was released yesterday to do hard labor, otherwise he would have been finished. However, when Shi left the inn, the other five people who had been detained on the same train were still being severely interrogated, and their fate was unknown. According to railway officials, passengers are detained on every passenger train. Because the railway bureau is under the oppressive power of the Japanese military, it cannot guarantee the safety of passengers.

Xin-Min County (100 li from Shenyang) As a result of negotiations with the railway bureau, the Japanese side has agreed to allow our armed railway police to be stationed to protect the railway and the armored trains will only go there. Except for the Japanese consulate, which has about a dozen Japanese soldiers, the county streets have become a free zone without any sign of soldiers or police. Therefore, bandits take the opportunity to rise up and openly plunder. Because the area is a buffer zone between the Chinese and Japanese troops, the Japanese artillery is stationed in Ju-Liu-He and is transferred back and forth to Shenyang every day, so the number of people increases and decreases. There are about one company. About 200 meters behind the station, dozens of newly built wooden barracks (about eight or nine of them have been completed). The rest are still under construction. Seven large-caliber heavy artillery pieces are erected next to the station. Two civilian boats and three small boats are moored on the west bank of Ju-Liu-He for the Japanese military to cross the river. The houses of the people on the shore by the railway have been occupied by the military. A cannon position has been set up on Nanshan on the east bank, the number is unknown, with electrical wires and sandbags installed. More than a dozen Japanese soldiers are digging semi-circular trenches on the north side. Further east to Ma-San-Jia, a company of Japanese cavalry is stationed, all living in Meng's shop.

Because of the prevalence of bandits in Huang-Gu-Tun, the Japanese military is on high alert near the station. Sandbags are piled up at intersections and pedestrians are occasionally searched, baring their chests to the cold wind, allowing them to search, which is very distressing. In the city and commercial port areas, merchants are still as before, only opening their doors and not lowering the window panels, and the business of food and groceries is still sufficient to maintain their expenses. As for foreign goods and consumable goods merchants, they spend their days idle, and no one consults them, and they all look up to the roof and sigh. If the current situation continues, I am afraid that by the end of the year, the entire city's commerce will inevitably come to an end. There are few pedestrians on the streets, and most of them are wearing white cloths on their arms. The desolate scene is unbearable to witness. After entering the city, I visited various friends, but most of them knocked on the doors ten times and no one opened them. Even those who had people watching at home were all panicked, as if a great disaster was about to befall them, making foreign travelers feel that they could not stay for a day. The most disturbing thing is that gunfire is heard everywhere at night. Currently, bandit robberies have spread from outside the city to inside the city and commercial port areas. In quiet streets and alleys, there are robberies after 4 or 5 pm. The Japanese military, in addition to closing the city gates early, has no other way to deal with it. The self-defense police, because they are ordered by the Japanese to return to the bureau in the evening, are not responsible for security, and the lives and property of the people are no longer guaranteed, so they are even more panicked than before. Until recently, foreign nationals from various countries have also moved out because they cannot live in peace, but the Japanese nationals have taken horse-drawn carriages to visit the city, and some have moved their families to the city, as a prelude to future co-residence. The Japanese flag flies everywhere in the city, and our blue and white national emblem can only be seen occasionally on the hats of the self-defense police, which is very sad. As for the brothels in the north and south markets and industrial areas, although they are sparsely visited, the Japanese side, in order to maintain the market, restricts them from leaving the area and strictly prohibits them. Those prostitutes who have no debts have already left the brothel, and those who remain in Shenyang are all poor and helpless creatures. Gambling dens and opium dens are everywhere in the northwest market and other places, and no one interferes with them. They can act freely and openly. The Japanese not only do not ban them, but also encourage them, their purpose being to expose the various shortcomings of the Chinese and make everyone addicted and unable to wake up, committing suicide. Their poisonous intentions are meticulous. On one hand, they send people to various important people's residences to search for weapons, and on the other hand, they force the people to hand them over, so the weapons of the Chinese are now all confiscated.

The strength of the bandits along the Ning-Lu Railway is unprecedented. When I went to Shenyang, about 13 li from Xin-Min, I saw several hundred bandits with complete weapons and horses, all dressed in short clothes, gathering in a willow forest more than a hundred paces from the railway. Fortunately, they did not harm the eastbound passenger train. The bandits erected a red flag with white characters on it, but because the road was far away, it was blurred and indistinguishable. Our military police were helpless because they were within the sphere of influence of the Japanese, and could only allow them to run rampant, and the travelers to and from suffered.

The Japanese military in Shenyang is extremely strict in censoring the newspapers of Tianjin and Beijing (also in Shanghai). Those who are found to be selling newspapers will be arrested. Those who are slightly guilty will be beaten and detained, and those who are seriously guilty will be killed with刺刀. Therefore, the residents of Shenyang are completely isolated from the outside world. The Japanese military police search for the Tianjin "Yi-Shi Daily" and "Ta-Kung-Pao" every day, and arrested the newspaper deliveryman of the Northeast Bookstore outside Xiaoxi Gate. The manager Shao Shang-wen was fortunate to have heard the news in advance and escaped, avoiding being killed. Many Chinese detectives are hired on the streets to侦察 the actions of newspaper vendors and passersby. The strictness of their surveillance can be imagined. However, the Japanese "Shun-Jing Times," "Manchuria Tai-Dong," and other newspapers can be sold freely and unhindered in western Liaoning, and no one resists them. The generosity of our compatriots is also very great.

In order to maintain the declining market, the Japanese side forcibly forces all entertainment venues to operate as usual. The people are worried and have no heart to be entertained. Therefore, theaters and theaters such as "Hui-Xian," "Da-Guan-Yuan," "Zhong-Shan," and "Gong-Yi" have been opened once, but because no one patronizes them, they cannot afford to lose money and have been suspended. Only tea houses and ballad books such as "Gong-Yu Hong-Tai-Xuan" can barely make a living because of their limited expenses. The hardship of these people is that they cannot quit because the Japanese side has imposed strict restrictions. They have the unspeakable suffering of a mute eating bitter melon.

The most active in the current political situation is Zhao Xin-bo, who holds the positions of Mayor of Shenyang, President of the Supreme Court, and President of the "Dong-San-Sheng Min-Bao" and "Xin-Min Evening News." Recently, he has also sought to replace the Chief of the Self-Defense Police Bureau. He holds several pseudo-positions and is the only favorite of the Japanese side. As for Yuan Jin-kai and Kan Chao-xi, they are not only puppets of the Japanese, but also Zhao's followers. They all want to take this opportunity to satisfy their official ambitions.

Regarding the so-called independence movement, the Japanese side is indeed actively instigating it. Their method is purely to use the shield of the enemy to attack the enemy. They first use the Chinese to take over various agencies, and the Japanese then insert themselves everywhere in the name of supervision, but in reality, they hold the power and control everything. Our crazy people are plotting to seize power and enter the political arena. Now that they have this opportunity, how can they not be used by others? It is rumored that the Japanese plan to secretly manipulate the establishment of the so-called new regime after the organization of various agencies is completed. The administrative power in name has been returned to China, adopting the old trick of destroying Korea. Currently, various political agencies in Shenyang have largely begun to work, and those that are less important are also actively proceeding. There are many who are coveting them. The people of the country should pay close attention to this situation. (October 28th)

Local dispatches

Fengxian 76

The regulations for the public clinic have been announced. The regulations for the public clinic have now been drafted by the county government and passed by the 67th county political conference, and have been approved by the Civil Affairs Office. They were officially announced the day before yesterday. The most important provisions are: (1) This clinic is established in accordance with the notice of the Department of Health and has been approved by the county council to implement social health and treat people's diseases as its purpose. (2) This clinic adopts a combination of Chinese and Western medicine to meet local needs. It specially hires Chinese and Western doctors to be responsible for diagnosis and treatment, and has an obstetrics department attached to ensure the safety of women's childbirth, with a chief midwife in charge. (3) This clinic may invite a number of local gentlemen to be hired by the county to organize an economic committee to promote the progress of the cause. (4) This clinic may accept the entrustment of the county government and local organs to handle various matters of inspection and testing and medical and health aspects. (5) The expenses of this clinic shall be decided by the county government. Before the local expenses have been subsidized, the county organs shall temporarily subsidize 120 yuan per month, and may collect donations from local funerals for application.

Shi-Niu-Tuan villagers were shot and injured by bandits. Qian Rong-tao, a farmer in Shi-Niu-Tuan, west of Qian-Jia-Qiao, in the fifth district of this county, is very poor and lives by farming. On the night of the 23rd of last month, five thugs suddenly came to the area, each holding guns and sticks. They dragged Qian Rong-tao from his bed and shot him, the bullet wounding his left eye. He fainted and fell to the ground. The bandits, seeing that they had succeeded, fled far away. Fortunately, the injury was not too serious and did not cause great harm. However, according to Qian's confession, he did not know any of the five bandits and had no enemies in the past. He really did not understand what their purpose was. His relatives and neighbors were also surprised. In addition to the county government sending police to limit the investigation, Qian himself has gone to Shanghai to seek medical treatment.

Songjiang 77

The Party Department mediates disputes among TCM organizations. In the county's TCM community, there are two organizations: the National Medicine Association and the TCM Association. According to regulations, only one organization is allowed to be organized in one place. However, the National Medicine Association has been approved by the County Party Department and recognized as a legitimate organization, while the TCM Association was initially delayed due to unclear organizational procedures. The general members were deeply resentful and once attacked each other. The local Party Department convened both parties for mediation, but it was difficult to reach an agreement. Yesterday, the Training Department of the Provincial Party Department sent a staff member, Mr. Wu, to Songjiang to work with the County Party Department to conduct reconciliation. Representatives from both parties, Zhu Wen-qing, Jiang An-ren, and others, discussed peace terms. It is rumored that the TCM Association will be reorganized, with members of the National Medicine Association as the initiators responsible for the preparations, to be completed within 20 days. The TCM organization dispute, which has lasted for more than a year, has come to an end.

Election fraud in the ninth district is being investigated. The citizens of the ninth district of this county have reported to the county court that there was various illegal fraud in the election of the head and deputy heads of townships in this session. The court summoned witnesses on the 3rd to open an investigation court. It is rumored that the evidence is conclusive and that the fact of stealing and using seals was discovered temporarily. The court ordered the accused, Jin Shou-lin, the former district chief, and Gu Zhong-rong, the township chief, to be released on bail. It is rumored that a public prosecution will be filed soon.

Suzhou 78

The murderer who assassinated Zhao has appealed to the court. Zhao Tie-qiao, the director of the Shanghai China Merchants Bureau, was assassinated at 8:00 a.m. on July 24th last year. Xia Shao-jin and Wang Jin-shan were captured by the Shanghai Municipal and County Public Security Bureaus one after another and sent to the Shanghai District Court for handling. The trial was concluded on June 25th of this year, and each was sentenced to death for premeditated murder. Xia and Wang refused to accept the sentence and appealed to the High Court. Yesterday (the 4th) at 2:00 p.m., Judge Hu of the Third Criminal Court opened the trial. The wife of the deceased, Zhao Wang-shi, was entrusted to attend the court by Deng Shu-kai, Zhao Tie-qiao's brother-in-law. Xia Shao-en and Wang Jin-shan both denied killing Zhao Tie-qiao. Deng Shu-kai testified that when Zhao Tie-qiao was shot, he was sent to the Bao-Long Hospital for treatment and said the phrase "Why make a fuss about nothing?" There were no other last words. After Judge Hu's testimony, he ordered a postponement of the trial because further investigation was needed. Xia and Wang were returned to custody.

Changshu 79

The principal of Yan-Xiang Elementary School died suddenly. There is an elementary school in Yan-Xiang, this county, which is a classroom, and there is only one teacher who handles all kinds of chores. The principal of the school, Hu Yan-lian, is a woman, 30 years old. Because her parents died early, she has not yet married. After graduating from Hu Ying-Hua Girls' School, she successively served as a teacher in various schools in this county. She only took the position of principal of the school this autumn. She is diligent in her duties on weekdays. On the 31st of last month, the children of the school went to school as usual, but did not see Principal Hu. It was not until 12:00 that the students returned home. The same thing happened the next day. The families of the students became suspicious and asked someone to go to the city to inquire at her uncle's house. According to him, he did not know either. He returned to the village to inspect the school, but Hu was sleeping on the floor. Therefore, the people of the village were quite surprised, because Hu was usually healthy and would not die suddenly. There were obviously suspicious points among them. Then her uncle, together with the dead person's cousin, Hu Tian-pu, went to the village to inspect. Unexpectedly, all the ornaments and various clothes in the dead person's clothing box were missing. The most bizarre thing was that four men's robes were found at the bottom of the box, so there were more doubts. At that time, because the body had been dead for a long time, they held a small funeral on the one hand, and Hu Tian-pu sent a petition to the county government and the Education Bureau, requesting a thorough investigation.

Wuxi 80

Counter-revolutionary criminals must not be sent to the Rehabilitation Institute hastily. Lin Biao, President of the Jiangsu Higher Court, said that after the opening of the Jiangsu Anti-Rebellion Institute, the prisons in various counties often requested that the counter-revolutionary criminals currently in custody be sent to the institute for rehabilitation without following the regulations of the Rehabilitation Institute, which was not in accordance with the regulations. Afterwards, all counter-revolutionary criminals who have committed ordinary crimes under investigation or trial cannot be sent to rehabilitation hastily. Even if the ordinary criminal case is concluded and the judgment is finalized, it should also be waited until the sentence of the ordinary criminal case is executed before the crime of counter-revolution is merged and executed. The county magistrate of this county, Chen Chuan-de, received this instruction yesterday (the 4th) and will comply with it.

A major fire in the Shen-Xin Spinning Factory. Shen-Xin Factory No. 3 of Xiao-Mu-Qiao, outside the west gate, was founded by the brothers Rong Zong-jing, who are giant merchants in this county. The business is very prosperous and profitable. At about 1:00 a.m. yesterday (the 4th), a fire suddenly broke out in the Yuan-Zi No. 1 flower stack in the factory. Suddenly, thick smoke filled the air, spewing through the roof. After the stack officer Jia Shi-pei noticed, he immediately sounded the alarm. After hearing the alarm, the fire brigades rushed to the scene to draw water for firefighting. After an hour, it was extinguished. It is estimated that seven houses were burned down, about 2,000 dan of lint cotton and seedless cotton, and 46 pieces of package paper (each piece is valued at 100 yuan). The total loss is more than 40,000 yuan. It is also rumored that the factory had just shipped 1,100 packages of cotton from Pinghu, Zhejiang, the day before the fire, which were also burned to ashes. The cause of the fire is unknown. Also, at Bao Wan-shun's Jewelry Store, Bao Wen-kui's residence next to Jie-Jing-Qiao Small Vegetable Market in Xia-Tang, outside the south gate, which are three rooms with two houses, the first house is a building, and the second house is a flat house. At noon and a half in the afternoon, a fire suddenly broke out in Bao's daughter-in-law's room on the upper floor, and the fire spread quite violently. As a result, all three rooms on the floor were burnt to the ground, and the loss reached more than 20,000 yuan.

Jiangyin 81

The Anti-Japanese Association seized a large batch of Japanese yarn again. The Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association reported the day before yesterday (the 2nd) that the Nan-Zha Public Welfare Cloth Factory privately imported a large batch of Japanese yarn. The Anti-Japanese Association sent personnel to the Public Welfare Cloth Factory and seized more than 700 packages of Japanese yarn. It also searched the Gao-Shen-Chang Cloth Store and seized more than 400 packages of Japanese yarn. At about 7 p.m. that night, they transported it to the Anti-Japanese Association for storage.

Changzhou 82

Inspect and seal up Japanese goods. After the warlord Zhou destroyed the county party headquarters and other three agencies, all industries have automatically sealed up Japanese goods and listed the Japanese goods to be reported to the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association for verification. The County Party Department convened a committee meeting on the 3rd and decided to order the Anti-Japanese Association to start inspecting and sealing up Japanese goods from now on. After receiving the order, the Anti-Japanese Association will immediately send out inspection teams to start work. The Education Bureau takes over the Women's Vocational School. Li Shou-qi, the principal of the Wu-Yi County Women's Vocational School, resigned and was approved by the County Bureau. Recently, the Director of the Education Bureau, Yang Hao-ming, has requested the county government to send the director to take over first. There were some twists and turns at the time. Later, Principal Li complied with the order to hand over the post. Director Yang then sent Sun Shi-ju yesterday to maintain everything.

Zhenjiang 83

Jiangning Finance Bureau Chief Investigated for Illegal Acts: Wang Shuren and other people from Jiangning County reported to the provincial government that Chen Rongshou, the head of the county's Finance Bureau, was smoking opium, engaging in embezzlement and malpractice, and holding multiple positions concurrently, thus tarnishing the Party's discipline. They specifically presented the provincial government with the various illegal activities of the bureau chief, requesting prompt removal and punishment and the appointment of a capable replacement. After receiving the report, the provincial government, if the allegations are true, deemed the behavior as illegal. The Finance Department was ordered to thoroughly investigate and await further instructions.

Various Trade Unions Will Form Volunteer Corps: The various trade unions in Zhenjiang County are organizing volunteer corps. Since the establishment of the volunteer corps preparatory office, led by Tao Shoubai, Sun Bin, and others, active preparations have been underway. A total of 128 individuals from various unions, including the Match Workers' Union, Transportation Workers' Union, Hotel Workers' Union, Gold and Silver Workers' Union, Incense Workers' Union, and Garment Workers' Union, have registered. The roster has been submitted to the county Party headquarters for review. Formal establishment will occur once approval for record-keeping is granted.

Nantong 84

Liability for Stolen Money in Bank Robbery: More than 26,000 yuan was stolen from the Nantong branch of the Bank of China. The funds were being transferred from Tailong Bank and were in the process of being counted when the robbery occurred. According to regulations, Tailong Bank is responsible for the lost funds. Tailong is an agency of the Bank of China and has reported the incident to Shanghai. The 280th Regiment stationed in Tong has apprehended one of the main suspects in the case, Ma Changgeng, who has been interrogated. A telegram has been sent to Chief Liang for instructions on punishment.

Disaster and Crop Failure in Funing Reclamation Area: The Funing Reclamation Area suffered a severe flood disaster. The farmlands of companies like Fuyu Ougeng and Dashun Qingyu were completely inundated. Thirty thousand tenant farmers are still trapped in the water and urgently need relief.

Qingjiang 85

Market Closure Continues Without Resolution: Cloth, general merchandise, and sundry goods shops in Huaiyin have been closed for four days as of today (the 31st). Although the county government sent officials such as Zhu Yayuan to persuade them to reopen, the merchants generally stated that financial difficulties were insurmountable, and many shop assistants had dispersed, making it difficult to resume business immediately. The Party headquarters telegraphed the provincial authorities yesterday, requesting instructions. The headquarters also intends to issue warnings to the closed shops, urging them to reopen as soon as possible to avoid further losses. However, the managers of the closed shops have reportedly been holding secret meetings at the money industry association for several days. Given this stalemate, a resolution seems distant.

Police Sub-Bureau Chiefs Demand Pay: Many chiefs and officers from the police substations of the Huaiyin Public Security Bureau went to the main bureau on the afternoon of the 30th, demanding four months' salary from July, August, September, and October of this year, as well as the remaining funds from the previous bureau chief, Zhao Zhenhua. The situation was chaotic. Acting Bureau Chief Zhang Quan addressed the crowd, promising to find a solution for relief in the shortest time possible, after which they dispersed.
