Huang Kangtun Discusses Overseas Chinese Education in Southeast Asia 87

Mr. Huang Kangtun, who has taught abroad for many years, recently returned from Southeast Asia. A reporter visited him at his residence and saw a flower basket on his table, dazzling like precious jade, containing coral rocks produced in the seas of Singapore. Mr. Huang taught at Penang Middle School for three years and Yangon Middle School for two years. He spoke in detail about the situation of the overseas Chinese communities in the British Straits Settlements and Burma. The reporter, considering the relevance of overseas Chinese education, arranged the following interview:

(Question) What is the current situation and effect of the prevalence of overseas Chinese schools? (Answer) The current situation of overseas Chinese schools cannot be fully described in a few words. In general, they are struggling in the recent economic downturn. One can say, "It is dark before dawn." The history of overseas Chinese schools is not long, with the oldest being no more than thirty years. After the dynastic change, they sprang up like mushrooms after rain. Mandarin Chinese is now commonly spoken in overseas Chinese communities in Singapore, Penang, and other ports. In recent years, the anti-Japanese movement's slogans, though not as loudly proclaimed or widely posted as in China, are more consistently and thoroughly boycotted than in China. The recent robbery in the Eastern Provinces and the expression of hot indignation and sorrow are particularly profound. These few points show that the latent growth of overseas Chinese education is an effect that cannot be ignored.

(Question) What is the degree of development of overseas Chinese secondary education? (Answer) Overseas Chinese primary schools are quite developed in various parts of Southeast Asia. Even in remote mountain and coastal villages, wherever there are dozens of Chinese shops, one can hear the "Three Principles of the People" anthem. However, secondary education, apart from the Chinese High School in Singapore, which has senior high school classes, only reaches the junior high school level in other cities. The scale, facilities, and student numbers are not as spacious and complete as the equivalent schools established by the British. However, they are more prominent than the various overseas Chinese primary schools. Taking the two middle schools where I (Mr. Huang) served, Penang and Yangon, the Penang school, although small, is full of vitality, and student development has reached capacity, making expansion necessary. The Yangon school is large in scale but lacks vitality, with few students. Recently, it has been temporarily suspended due to various problems. The biggest reason for the success or failure of these two schools is the geographical location of Penang, which attracts students from various foreign ports. Students come from as far north as Siam and Burma, as far south as Kuala Lumpur and other small towns in the Malay Peninsula, and as far west as Sumatra. Therefore, student development is strong, and the school foundation is easily consolidated. Although Yangon is the capital of Burma and has the only middle school for the 300,000 overseas Chinese in Burma, the number of students in Chinese schools in each town is not very large, making it difficult for middle school graduates to develop. However, given the school's location and the dilapidated state of its buildings, it may be possible to convert it into an overseas Chinese public school, from kindergarten to co-educational primary school, merging the existing Chinese schools in Yangon that are currently too small. Then, gradually restoring it would be a great prospect.

(Question) Given the large number of overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia, their strong financial resources, and the considerable history of running their own schools, why has no university been established? (Answer) From the perspective of the actual needs of the number of overseas Chinese and their social culture, it is necessary to build a university. Economically, it is also possible to establish one. For example, the University of Yangon in Burma and Raffles University in Singapore, though established by the British, have received substantial donations from the overseas Chinese community. The reason why they are willing to help others but hesitant to build their own is that, firstly, there is a lack of qualified personnel with a strong reputation in China to call for overseas Chinese participation. Secondly, wealthy overseas Chinese who have lived abroad for a long time tend to admire Western education, sending their children to English schools from a young age and then studying in England and America to gain local recognition. Those who admire their motherland often send their children to study in China after graduating from primary school, lacking confidence in the local Chinese secondary schools. Thirdly, prominent and wealthy individuals in the overseas Chinese community often pursue different paths, lacking the spirit of cooperation and strong organizational skills. Therefore, there is no initiative to automatically establish a higher education institution. In fact, university education should be adapted to local conditions. The number of Caucasians in Southeast Asia is only a fraction of the total population, yet the construction of higher education is progressing rapidly, and students of all races, including Chinese, Malay, and Indian, are enrolled. However, Caucasians themselves are often unwilling to let their children study with people of color from the colonies. We are simply neglecting our own fields and cultivating others' fields, which is regrettable.

Local News

Wang Boling to Assume Position as Director of Student Military Training on the 7th 88

(Guomin She) Since the Japanese invasion of the Eastern Provinces, all major schools in the city have organized volunteer corps. To unify training, the Central Committee has appointed Mr. Wang Boling as the director of the student volunteer corps training center in the city. Yesterday, a reporter from Guomin She met with Mr. Wang at the municipal government. Mr. Wang is scheduled to be sworn in on the 7th (this Saturday at 10:00 AM) in the auditorium of Jiangwan Labor University. Leaders from the city's Party, government, and military, as well as presidents of major schools, will be invited to attend the ceremony. The training center's office will be located in the Labor University library. The training guidelines will be based on the central government's recently promulgated student volunteer corps training program, adapted to the specific circumstances of Shanghai schools. The Central Training Supervisory Department has newly appointed over a hundred instructors from more than fifty schools, who will arrive in Shanghai tomorrow morning (today) and report to their respective schools according to the assigned list. High school students and above will be called student volunteer corps, while junior high school students will be called young pioneer volunteer corps. Female students, due to physical limitations, will not receive the same military training as male students. Plans are underway to provide them with easier military exercises.

Mayor Zhang Invited Presidents of Major Schools to Talk Yesterday 89

(Guomin She) Since the central government appointed Mr. Wang Boling as the director of the student volunteer corps training center in the city, Mr. Wang rushed from Beijing to Shanghai to prepare everything. To facilitate Mr. Wang's contact with the presidents of various schools, Mayor Zhang Yuejun invited the presidents of universities and middle schools in the city to a meeting at the municipal government auditorium at 2:00 PM yesterday. The university presidents present included Chu Minyi (Zhongfa), Pan Gongzhan, Li Zhaohuan (Zhonggong), Hu Shuhua (Jiaoda), Xu Peikun (Tongji), and Tang Demin (Zhongda), representing Shen Junru (Jinan) and Lin Jiyong (Law School). The middle school presidents present included Tao Baichuan, Wang Xiaoying, Xu Wentai, and a representative from Fudan Middle School, totaling over fifty people. The Director of the Municipal Education Bureau, Xu Peihuang, was also present. Mayor Zhang chaired the meeting. First, Mayor Zhang introduced Mr. Wang Boling. Then, Mr. Wang reported on the central government's attention to student organization of volunteer corps and the process of appointing himself as the training director. He also hoped that the school presidents would contribute to military training. Later, Shen Junru, Lin Jiyong, Wang Xiaoying, and others expressed their opinions successively. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM.

(4) To borrow 500 yuan from the Municipal Party Headquarters to meet urgent needs. The resolution was passed. (5) The scope of fundraising will be based on (a) Party, government, and military agencies, (b) commercial and financial institutions, (c) individuals, and (d) faculty and staff of various schools. The resolution was passed. (6) To draft a fundraising appeal, Daxia was appointed to draft it. (7) The fundraising period is limited to two weeks. The resolution was passed. (8) The committee will not temporarily assign positions, and all matters will be the responsibility of the entire committee. The resolution was passed. (9) The meeting schedule of the committee will be convened temporarily by the chairman. (10) The committee should draft simple rules. Hard Court Tennis Doubles Semi-Finals, the Two Zhengs Fail at the Last Moment 95

Zheng Zhaojia's Partner is Slightly Inferior

The Defeat of the Two Zhengs

Klinov 3-6 Zheng Zhaojia

8-6

Tuina 6-2 Zheng Yuankai

Seventeen Mile Second Trial Run 97

Shi Jinsheng Sets New Record

Time: Two Hours and Twenty-Seven Minutes

Alarming the Entire City

The annual Shanghai International Walking Competition has been dominated by the Chinese team for three consecutive years. To maintain this past glory, they must prepare in advance. With the competition scheduled for the 6th of next month, preparations are rapidly approaching completion. A second full-length seventeen-mile hard training session was held the day before yesterday (1st). Veteran team member Shen Zengjue is far away in Ningbo, and strong contender Lü Wenxia was unable to participate due to other commitments. Zhang Zao Cun, one of the pioneers of the sport, was also unable to revive his form due to being busy. Furthermore, Zhou Yuyu, the international champion, has no intention of joining again. This year, the team's overall strength will be affected. However, veteran athletes Shi Jinsheng, Zhang Zaojiu, Hou Genren, Xie Xingdao, Zhou Ruquan, as well as newcomers Lü Wenxia, Xu Luchen, Lü Chongyi, and others, totaling more than twenty people, have been diligently training daily to seize victory. More than forty people participated on this day, and Yao Shuen and Wang Mingzhi, who had not been present for some time, also joined in. In the end, about thirty people reached the finish line. The results of the top ten are listed below:

Page 11

Free Talk

The Voice of Resistance Against Japan

— Xianxiang

Nietzsche said it well: "You must seek out your enemies. You must wage your wars." I do not urge you to work. I urge you to fight. I do not urge you to seek peace. I urge you to seek victory. Make your work a war." Nietzsche was a famous modern philosopher in Germany. His philosophy of the Superman had a great influence on the German national character. I feel that a large nation like ours, situated in East Asia where justice is disregarded and Japanese pirates run rampant, should promote this kind of active and enterprising spirit.

Do not talk about the arts until the weeds are removed from the yard.

Edison Besieged From All Sides 98

A dispatch from Wilmington on October 30th from the National Press states: Edison's will stipulates that assets of the Edison Company, worth approximately $14 million USD, are to be given entirely to the children of his second wife. The house only will be converted into a trust fund, with the interest distributed to the six children of his first wife. William, the son of the first wife, now claims that he will contest this in court... Chinese old scholars generally criticized after reading this telegram, saying, "Edison probably didn't go to university, so he's caused this mess. The Great Learning clearly states, 'Investigate things, then knowledge extends; knowledge extends, then intentions are sincere; intentions are sincere, then the heart is rectified; the heart is rectified, then the person is cultivated; the person is cultivated, then the family is regulated; the family is regulated, then the state is rightly governed; the state is rightly governed, then the whole kingdom is made tranquil and happy.' Who told him to only investigate things and not regulate his family?"

Socialists also do not spare him. They say:

"Money belongs to society. You should pass it from father to son, son to grandson. Money is like fertilizer; piling too much on a seedling will burn it to death. You're piling 14 million US dollars on one child of your second wife, loving him but actually harming him. You're practically telling him to take that inexhaustible wealth to indulge in eating, drinking, gambling, and prostitution, burying your beloved son alive in a land of ease. William is also useless. You should learn from your father to invent and create, not freeload off him. Inheriting an inheritance is already useless enough; how much worse is it to fight with your brother over the inheritance? That is even more useless." In short, passing on industry to descendants is the stupidest thing to do. Edison was an exceptionally intelligent man, yet in dealing with his inheritance, he was as foolish as Li Hongzhang and Sheng Xuanhuai, causing his own flesh and blood to start lawsuits and letting lawyers get rich. This is beyond my expectations.

Miscellaneous Notes on the Hawaiian Islands 99

— Zheng Zhaoxi

The Hawaiian Islands are located in the Pacific Ocean. They are shaped like a string of pearls, consisting of eight islands of varying sizes. The area is 6,600 square miles. The islands are rich in agricultural products and have excellent scenery. They are known as the paradise of the Pacific. Although the location is in the tropics, the climate is moderated by the ocean. It is not hot at all in summer. In recent years, many people travel there to escape the heat. It is said that the administrative rights of the islands were originally held by local chieftains. In 1898, the influence of the United States expanded into the territory, and it became a possession. Later, people with aspirations repeatedly sought independence but failed. Liang Qichao traveled to the United States in 1899 and recorded a section in his diary with many feelings:

"...The former queen of the islands now lives in Washington, D.C., as a commoner. The country has been handed over to others. The bright moon shines on the former country, and it is unbearable to look back. Reading Li Houzhu's lines of 'tears wash my face,' onlookers are still saddened. I wonder what the lady, living alone, thinks in her heart. Alas. Nothing is more poignant than the lane of the Black Coats, which is now a newly painted beam in another family's home. How beautiful is this paradise in the Pacific, but unfortunately, those who enjoy it are not the rulers of that capital... "

Alas. Ren Gong is indeed a sentimental person and also deeply patriotic. Now seeing others lose their country and land, he still grieves on behalf of others. At this time, how could he have known that forty years later, China would also be forced into this situation? If he knew in the afterlife, I wonder how extreme his grief would be. (Que Chou)

Remembering Li Zhongjie, Who Died in the Sino-Japanese War 100

— Shouman

In the twentieth year of the Guangxu reign, our country sent troops to aid Korea due to internal unrest, and war broke out with Japan. At that time, many of our country's generals were arrogant and complacent, which ultimately led to the complete defeat of both the naval and land forces. They ceded territory to seek peace and bowed their heads in submission to the lewd power of the Japanese slaves. The shame can be said to be extreme. At that time, there was a man named Li Zhi, whose courtesy name was Zhongjie, from Jintan, Jiangsu. He graduated from the Beiyang Naval Academy and later served as the chief mate of the Yongjing warship. When the Sino-Japanese War broke out in 1894, he concurrently served as the garrison commander of the left and right wings of the navy. In the sea area of ​​the Yellow Sea, he fought fiercely with the Japanese army for several days and nights without ever retreating. At that time, our country's fleet was largely sunk by the enemy due to improper measures. Although the Yongjing warship was fortunate enough to survive, the enemy was numerous and we were few, and it was not easy to fight. Li had no choice but to say to his subordinates: "Today, we will die whether we fight or not. Rather than waiting to die with our hands tied, it is better to fight to the death. I hope everyone will work hard and not be afraid anymore." Thereupon, the crowd was moved to tears. Li personally operated the artillery and launched a fierce attack on the enemy. The Japanese warships fired several cannons at the same time, and the Yongjing warship was hit and sunk. None of the officers and soldiers survived. Alas, how valiant.

Strange Tales of Bestiality 101

— Jing Mengdie

Outside the east gate of Jintan, there is a town called Yaotang. Five miles southwest of Yaotang, there is a small village located in a remote and secluded place, rarely visited by people, commonly called Evil Dog Village. There are no more than ten families in the village, and every family raises dogs. The dogs' nature is particularly fierce and cruel. The owners use them to guard against thugs and petty thieves. Usually, beggars warn each other not to enter the village. Even passersby must first ask the villagers to guide and protect them. The dogs in the village also have special characteristics. They are particularly fond of eating dead human flesh. Almost none of the new graves in the surrounding area with coffins exposed above ground are intact. Often, late at night, the dogs find a coffin. They strike it on the head and break it open, then stick their heads in, drag out the corpse, and devour it together. When the villagers go to check the next morning, only scattered white bones remain. One cool autumn night, a fisherman named Jia set up his net on the riverbank outside the village, working as a fisherman. In the middle of the night, he felt tired and wanted to sleep. He saw a small boat left by water chestnut pickers on the beach next to him. Jia went into it to take a nap and unknowingly fell asleep. Unexpectedly, the dogs saw it and mistook the boat for a coffin and Jia for a dead person. They went forward and fiercely bit his head, dragging him out of the boat. Jia woke up in extreme pain and fought with the dogs, shouting for help. The villagers heard the noise, woke up in alarm, gathered together, and came to his rescue. But Jia's face was already blurred, and blood made him unrecognizable. At dawn, he was carried to the town for medical treatment. My friend, Mr. Mou, happened to be in the town at that time. He saw the situation, felt strange, and questioned him to find out the details. He told me about it, and it was no different from the "wild dogs" mentioned in Liao Zhai. Alas, it is commonly said that there is an Evil Dog Village in the underworld. Unexpectedly, it is actually in the human world. Then, is there truly a hell in the human world?

In my hometown town (in the eastern countryside of Danyang), there is a tofu shop surnamed Yu. The shop kept a male donkey to replace human labor. The donkey's nature was strangely lewd. When grinding, even if its eyes were covered, it would stop working and become violent as soon as it heard a woman's voice. Therefore, the female owner dared not get close to it. One day, it was tied outside the door. A young woman from the countryside went to the market to shop and passed in front of it on her way home. The donkey saw her, forcefully broke its rope, and chased after the woman. The woman ran wildly and was eventually caught by it. The donkey bit her hair with its mouth and used its two feet to pounce on her shoulders. People in the market who saw this clapped their hands and laughed. When the owner heard about it and came to the rescue, the woman's skirt was torn, her skin was broken, and blood was flowing between her thighs. This was because it was the season for wearing thin autumn clothing, so she was easily injured. The woman was both distressed and ashamed, so she summoned her husband to seriously negotiate with the shop owner. After the Yu family provided medical treatment and apologized, the matter was settled. When I returned home and heard about it, I remembered the donkey disaster cases recorded in the notes of ancient people. I then believed that it was not untrue. It is also a strangeness of bestiality.

Records of Sights and Sounds in the Old Capital 103

— Zhu An

Tour Guides

In the capitals of Eastern and Western civilized countries, there are guidebooks. Beiping is the cultural center of our country. People from far and near hear of it and admire it, and millions of people wish to visit. Yet, there is ultimately no book that can guide tourists. How strange is that? From the Records of Things Seen in the Capital, there are countless books that research the historical sites of Yandu. However, these can provide resources for scholars to explore, but they cannot serve as a guide for tourists. Tourists do not have the time to read them. There are also many works by Westerners describing Beijing, but they are ultimately alienated and do not match the recent situation. Recently, Chen Zongfan from Fujian compiled three volumes of A Comprehensive Study of Yandu, which describes the inner and outer neighborhoods, gardens, and historical sites of Zhou, and uses recent events to prove them. This can be a practical resource, but it is still mostly focused on historical sites and not specifically written as a tour guide. Matters such as markets, trade, food, and recreation are not included in the plan. The guidebooks published in the market are bland and tasteless, and insufficient to evoke the feeling of sightseeing. In the spring of the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, the Municipal Government's Prosperity Design Committee planned to write a book to meet this need. The draft had already been prepared, but the political situation changed, and it was shelved. Furthermore, the committee believed that Westerners who came to visit were unfamiliar with the place and often hired open-air interpreters near the Beijing Hotel as travel companions. These people were ignorant and knew nothing about historical sites. They repeated errors and perpetuated falsehoods, which brought shame to the country. It was proposed to open a training institute to cultivate such talents. This matter also ultimately came to nothing. Now, hundreds of American tour groups come every year. Even if the Municipal Government can send personnel to receive them, it is impossible to explain to them one by one. The civic groups have not yet developed and do not have the ability to fulfill the duties of the host. Think about those who travel thousands of miles to see the glory of the country. Entering this famous capital, there is no one there. They do not know where to go, nor do they know what to buy. They are at a loss and follow others, their eyes are dazzled by the five colors, like the deaf and blind. They cannot name anything and leave. What will their impressions be afterward? Thinking about this, one can only sigh deeply. Now the Municipal Government always complains about the lack of funds. Think about how every tourist who comes must spend at least 100 yuan in Beiping. This 100 yuan is the floating capital of the city of Beiping. The City Chamber of Commerce, in order to receive the incoming capital, should cooperate with the Municipal Government to create a large-scale hospitality agency. It should specialize in taking goods that can cater to the tastes of Westerners, display them with the inherent artistic spirit of our country, mark the prices in European languages, and hire people with new commercial knowledge who can speak European languages to be responsible for reception. Even with the profits, there would be ample surplus to manage the above-mentioned two matters. Why worry about the lack of funds? Some say that in the spring of the twentieth year, the European and American Alumni Association held an arts and crafts exhibition, but the gains were small. This matter is probably not easy to do. However, one does not know that what is displayed should not be limited to arts and crafts. One can collect everything that is a special product of our country, including food, clothing, and playthings. If one only seeks to sell high-priced treasures, it will be difficult. This naturally depends on merchants taking the initiative and the government providing guidance and assistance. It is not too late to catch up quickly.

The Devil Angel. The day and night shows are full. This film is about the nature of war, so it can cater to the audience's psychology.

The concentration point of small newspaper vendors is on Rue du Lieutenant Petiot. Its remaining veins extend south to the intersection of Peng Road and north to Dade Lane.

A Country Bumpkin Comes to Shanghai Again (7) 104

— Bao Tianxiao

He was talking to himself, and no one paid attention to him. The friend sitting across from him was reading the newspaper, finishing the main section and then looking at the accompanying pictorial. The country bumpkin was still looking at his side, not thinking that his eyes were shooting over. Suddenly, he jumped up and said:

"It's revolting! It's revolting! This world is really revolting! -" Everyone in the third-class carriage was startled by his shouting, not knowing what was the reason. Could a country old man have a mental illness? Everyone came to ask him what was the matter?

"This world is really revolting." He still shook his head and sighed, then said: "No wonder Ashui and Jinduniang said Shanghai is not a good place. They've even published erotic picture books."

"Where is there any erotic picture book?" The gentleman sitting across from him initially had his face covered by the newspaper, and the country bumpkin hadn't seen him clearly. Now, he saw a young man who looked like a university student. "You're still saying it's not an erotic picture book?" The country bumpkin pointed at the pictorial in the young man's hand. "Aren't there photos of naked girls printed on it? With big boobs sticking out and big butts sticking out. Do you think I, a country bumpkin, can't see this clearly?"

It turned out that the pictorial was printing a famous painting of a beautiful nude by the French Baron and several photos of recent female swimmers. Although they were all wearing swimsuits, their shapely breasts naturally protruded in front. People in Shanghai were already accustomed to it, and those photographed girls were already generous and shameless, but it shocked the country old man.

"This is called art. This is called human beauty, the beauty of curves. You don't understand that." The young man naturally had to defend the pictorial.

"I certainly don't understand. Is this called art? Thank you – I never believe that you have to take off your pants to be considered beautiful. You said many things about beauty, many things about beauty, and I can't remember many. If not wearing pants is considered beautiful, then everyone on this train should take off their pants. Why don't we all come and be beautiful together?" The country bumpkin became more and more energetic, and he was about to say all kinds of nonsense.

"Only when beautiful people are naked does their beauty show. Not just anyone can show beauty. Like you, a country old man, with a haggard and withered body, can you say you have any curves or human beauty after you're naked?" The young man also refused to give way in words.

"I am naturally a haggard and withered old man and have no beauty. Well then, you're a fair and plump young man. You can take off your pants and let people see your beauty." At this time, the country bumpkin also became angry.

Russian Wheat Harvest is Poor and the Flour Market Rebounds 115

According to the general people's speculation, the turning point of the European and American wheat markets is because of the poor harvest in Russia, and powerful selling pressure can be avoided. If this is true, then the foreign wheat in China may have to stop temporarily. For this reason, the hearts of people inside and outside the industry have become more stable. As a result, there was no change in this month, 5 li in December, and 2 or 4 points in January and February respectively.

Until the opening in the afternoon, it still made up for the floating short, and the temporary speculation absorbed it quite smoothly, and the market gradually rose. Looking at the later steps, if there is no special change in foreign wheat, it may have to rise a little bit. As a result, this month was 1 point better than the previous day, December, January and February were 1 point smaller, March was 2 points better and April was not moving.

Beijing and Guangdong Representatives Held the Sixth Preparatory Meeting Yesterday 124

Beijing Representatives First Exchanged Opinions After Arriving in Shanghai

A Conversation Was Held in the Morning and the Sixth Meeting Was Held in the Afternoon

The Discussion on the Fourth Plenary Session Problem Was Not Completed and the Meeting Was Temporarily Extended

Waiting for the Reply from Guangdong, the Meeting Can Continue This Morning

Guangdong Representatives Plan to Propose a Proposal to Protect People's Freedom

Since the morning of the 1st, the Beijing and Guangdong representatives have exchanged opinions on party affairs issues in the conversation meeting. As a result, both parties agreed to temporarily formulate three items regarding the opening method of the Fourth Plenary Session. The Beijing representatives immediately went to Beijing that night to ask for instructions, and the meeting was temporarily adjourned. At 8:00 a.m. yesterday, the Beijing representatives Zhang Jingjiang, Zhang Ji, Wu Tiecheng, accompanied by Yu Youren, Shao Lizi, He Yingqin, etc., returned to Shanghai. At 10:30 a.m. yesterday, all the Beijing and Guangdong representatives held a conversation meeting at Wu's residence. Yu Youren, Shao Lizi, He Yingqin, Zhu Peide, etc. also attended. It was not until 12:00 that it ended. The result was still satisfactory. The atmosphere of the peace meeting showed a turning point. At 4:30 p.m., the Beijing and Guangdong representatives formally held the Sixth Preparatory Meeting and adjourned at 6:00 p.m. The content of the discussion was still focused on the issue of the opening method of the Fourth National Congress. The Beijing representatives conveyed the will of Beijing, accepted the first item of the three temporarily set methods, and the Guangdong representatives agreed to telegraph Guangdong for instructions, and then announced the adjournment. It was decided to continue the Sixth Preparatory Meeting at 10:00 a.m. this morning. At that time, the reply from Guangdong should arrive and the discussion will continue. Now I will describe what I heard yesterday as follows:

Negotiation Process of the Party Affairs Case 125

Both parties' representatives believe that the party affairs issue is very important. This time, there should be a precise discussion to seek concrete measures to prevent internal disputes in the party in the future. Therefore, the two parties' representatives conducted two studies at Wu's residence on July 31 and this month's 1st, and then agreed on three methods for the Fourth National Congress: (1) The representatives of both parties will merge and hold a meeting; (2) Beijing and Guangdong will hold meetings at the same time, but the list of the Fourth Central Executive and Supervisory Committee members will be agreed upon by both parties first, and then passed by both parties' conferences; (3) The conference will be postponed until next year. After the above three methods were agreed upon, the representatives of both parties reported to the central government for instructions and chose one to handle. The Guangdong representatives used telegrams to ask for instructions, and the Beijing representatives took advantage of the preparatory meeting's adjournment to recommend Zhang Ji, Zhang Jingjiang, Wu Tiecheng, and Chen Mingshu to go to Beijing in person to ask the central government for instructions. After Zhang Ji and others reported to Beijing, after discussions among the various committees of the central government, it was decided to adopt the first method, with all the representatives of both parties attending and merging the meetings. In case the Guangdong Plenary Session representatives do not arrive before the 12th, it is possible to hold the opening ceremony on the 12th first, and the conference can be delayed for a few days to allow the Guangdong Plenary Session representatives to arrive. Zhang Ji and others brought this mission back to Shanghai the night before yesterday. When they arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning, they went to Wu Tiecheng's mansion on Haige Road to hold a preliminary meeting. In addition to the five representatives Zhang Ji, Zhang Jingjiang, Wu Tiecheng, Cai Yuanpei, and Chen Mingshu, there were also Yu Youren, Shao Lizi, Zhu Peide, He Yingqin, etc. After discussing for two hours, they all agreed to make this meeting a complete success. At 10 o'clock, they went to Wu's residence with the Guangdong representatives to hold a conversation meeting.

Conversation Meeting at Wu's Residence in the Morning 126

Before the conversation meeting was held, the Guangdong representatives also held a meeting once. After receiving the notice from the Beijing representatives, they arrived at Ren Wu's residence on Gordon Road one after another at about 10 o'clock to prepare for the meeting. At 10:25, the Beijing representatives and others arrived at the meeting from Wu's residence on Haige Road. After the representatives of both parties arrived, they began an informal discussion at 10:30. In addition to the Guangdong representatives Wang Jingwei, Sun Ke, Chen Youren, Li Wenfan, Zou Lu, Wu Chaochu, and the Beijing representatives Zhang Ji, Wu Tiecheng, Cai Yuanpei, Zhang Jingjiang, and Chen Mingshu, Central Committee members Yu Youren, He Yingqin, Zhu Peide, Shao Lizi, etc. also participated in the discussion. It lasted about one and a half hours until 12:00 noon. As a result, according to the Beijing and Guangdong representatives Zhang Ji, Sun Ke, etc., they are still exchanging views based on the three methods temporarily formulated in the first conversation meeting to solve the problem of the opening of the Fourth Plenary Session.

The Sixth Meeting is Postponed 127

At the conversation meeting at Wu's residence yesterday morning, it was decided to hold the Sixth Preparatory Meeting of the Beijing and Guangdong representatives at 4:00 p.m. yesterday. At that time, Wang Jingwei, Sun Ke, etc. arrived at Wu's residence first. Before long, the Beijing representatives also arrived one after another. The meeting was held at 4:30. The attending representatives were Cai Yuanpei, Zhang Ji, Zhang Jingjiang, Chen Mingshu, Wu Tiecheng, Wang Jingwei, Sun Ke, Li Wenfan, Zou Lu, Wu Chaochu, and Chen Youren. Wang Jingwei was elected as the temporary chairman. After the etiquette was completed, the discussion began. It was completely focused on the issue of the opening method of the Fourth National Congress. First, the Beijing representatives relayed the will of Beijing. After detailed discussions between the two parties, the opinions were still not consistent. The Guangdong representatives, etc., reported the three methods decided in the conversation meeting on the 1st to Guangdong without a reply, so they immediately reported the will of Beijing to the Guangdong Central Party Headquarters and asked for instructions on everything. After the reply arrived, a decision was made, and the adjournment was announced. It was decided to continue the Sixth Preparatory Meeting at 9:30 a.m. or 10:30 a.m. this morning. If there is still no reply from Guangdong at that time, a meeting will also be held.

Important Talks by Various Central Committee Members 128

The three committee members, He Yingqin, Zhu Peide, and Shao Lizi, came to Shanghai by car together yesterday morning (4th) and went to Wu's residence on Haige Road to talk with the central representatives. Committee member Yu Youren also arrived, and then went to Wu's residence on Gordon Road to participate in the conversation meeting of both parties. A reporter then met with the four gentlemen and asked about their feelings about the prospects for peace. The four gentlemen were all optimistic, because the crux of the current meeting has entered the problem of the Fourth National Congress. In the two conversation meetings on the 31st and 1st, three plans were drawn up: (1) The two parties of Beijing and Guangdong will gather to hold a meeting; (2) The two parties of Beijing and Guangdong will hold meetings separately, but they will act in a spirit of cooperation; (3) Postpone the meeting and select another representative. The four representatives Zhang Chen Zhang Wu entered Beijing on the evening of the 1st to ask the central government for instructions on this. After the decision was made to adopt the first method, because only this party can fully express the true unity to deal with the current national crisis. At first, there were concerns that there were too many people and there was no such large venue, but in order to promote unity, all difficulties were eliminated. The number of representatives from Guangdong was not limited, and the whole group gathered to hold a meeting. The original date of the meeting was November 12, and it was impossible to change the views of rushing to the national crisis and expressing unity, but it was feared that the representatives from Guangdong could not arrive in full. It is proposed to postpone the formal meeting for a few days after the opening ceremony. This afternoon, this decision will be submitted to the preparatory meeting for consultation. Both parties are sincerely seeking the unity of the party, and they are deeply convinced that a satisfactory result will be obtained.

New Proposal from the Guangdong Representative 129

The Far East News Agency reports that Guangdong representatives Wang Jingwei and others, after the passage of the reform proposal for the central political system, drafted a bill to protect the freedom and rights of the people. Due to consecutive adjournments, it was not submitted. Yesterday, at the sixth preparatory meeting, both parties focused on the issue of the Fourth National Congress and it was not discussed. It is reported that when the meeting opens today, they plan to submit it. A reporter from the Far East News Agency learned yesterday that the gist of the proposal is to prevent the abuse of military power, indiscriminate arrests and punishments of the people, which would create resentment and hinder party governance. The articles stipulating the protection of the people's freedom and rights are as follows: First, the people shall not be arrested, tried, or punished by any military organs or military tribunals, except as stipulated by martial law. Second, party departments at all levels shall not arrest or punish the people, confiscate property, or close down people's business or non-business organizations. Third, the people have freedom of assembly, and shall not be interfered with if they do not carry weapons or directly disrupt social order. Fourth, the people may freely express their opinions through speech, writing, drawing, and other methods. Various printed materials shall not be banned from distribution unless convicted by a court, except for printed materials without a responsible person.

Finance Minister Song Ziwen, when he was in Shanghai, once visited Wang Jingwei with Yu Youren and Chen Guofu to inquire about his attitude towards Chiang and Hu. Wang expressed his maintenance of his original position, and they parted without results. According to those close to Wang and Hu, when Wang Jingwei first visited Hu Hanmin, they met and shed tears, sighing incessantly. Afterwards, Wang repeatedly stated that he would follow Hu's lead in everything. Wang and Hu agreed that no matter what, they would never leave Shanghai. Li Jishen is still staying in Shanghai. Rumors that he had recently returned to Guangdong are not true. It was also said that Huang Shaoxiong would return to Guangdong within days after the Guangdong representatives arrived in Shanghai, but according to Huang's aides, this is also inaccurate, and Huang has no such intention at present. Ju Zheng is suffering from severe typhoid fever, with temperatures often above 100 degrees. He has been moved to the Sino-Western Sanatorium for treatment. Doctors say he is still in a critical condition and has prohibited visitors.

Telegram from Teachers and Staff of Secondary Schools 132

The teachers and staff of secondary schools in Shanghai sent a telegram to promote peaceful unification, saying: "To Mr. Chiang Kai-shek in Nanjing, Mr. Hu Zhantang, Mr. Wang Jingwei, Mr. Cai Zimin, Mr. Sun Zhesheng, Mr. Zhang Jingjiang, Mr. Wu Chaochu, Mr. Li Shizeng, Mr. Chen Youren, Mr. Zhang Puquan, Mr. Zou Haibin, Mr. Chen Zhenru, Mr. Li Wenfan, Mr. Wu Tiecheng in Shanghai: Since the founding of the Republic of China, our people have been hoping and disappointed every day. The Qing Dynasty was bad, and there was the Xinhai Revolution. At that time, the people of the whole country believed that after the revolution, the country would become rich and strong day by day. The desire for good governance was indescribable. Unexpectedly, in the past ten years, Yuan Shikai proclaimed himself emperor, Zhang Xun restored the monarchy, the Anfu clique harmed the country, Cao Kun bribed votes, warlords divided the country, and wars continued for years. The country's affairs deteriorated, and the National Revolution arose. When the National Revolutionary Army launched the Northern Expedition, it left Shaoguan, went down to Nanchang, conquered Wuhan, captured Nanjing, took Jinan, and reached Peiping. In less than two years, the Northern Warlords were almost completely wiped out. The people, who had been disappointed for a long time, cheered wildly, and their hopes for the future of the National Revolution surpassed those of the Xinhai Revolution. How could they know that after four years, the war would not end, and the great plan of political tutelage has not yet been realized. Now, refugees are everywhere, and the violent Japanese invade the country's life. The national spirit is in imminent danger, and the people's mentality can be said to have gone from disappointment to despair. Recently, party and government officials also know that peaceful unification cannot be delayed any longer. Therefore, the peace conference is held in Shanghai. Although the people are in despair, they still see this as a glimmer of hope for the country. However, judging from the situation in recent days, the future of the peace conference is difficult to be optimistic about. We believe that since the party and government officials are all believers in the Three Principles of the People and have all received the Premier's will to work hard for the National Revolution, since they hold the same doctrine and want to achieve the same goal, what contention is still unresolved and cannot be understood? Political views and policies are by no means absolutely good or bad. If the officials are truly for the country and the people, there must be room for negotiation and consensus. Otherwise, our people will recognize that what the officials are fighting for must be private interests, and they will not be able to understand the officials. The officials may have followed the Premier, devoted themselves to the revolution, or dedicated themselves to the party and the country, and served on the battlefield. Their love for the country is something that we and others cannot match. In the face of national crisis, there is no reason to remain indifferent. If they are still fighting for private interests, then the country will be destroyed and the family will perish together. The officials are wise and must know this. Seeing the country on the verge of collapse, we can no longer remain silent. We sincerely hope that the officials will unite quickly, secure the country internally and resist foreign aggression, and jointly seek the prosperity and strength of the country. Those who do not hesitate to undermine peaceful unification are truly sinners of the nation, and the people of the country should rise up and denounce them." Jointly signed by the teachers and staff of secondary schools in Shanghai (with the names of 772 people omitted).

Employees, through the procedures of the border team, and have a family approval certificate, can all be members of this team. The Municipal Government Submitted a Written Protest Regarding the Incident of Japanese Sailors Robbing Goods 141

Divided into four points: punishment of the murderers, compensation, apology, and guarantee

Mayor Zhang said that he could not interfere by force

Regarding the incident on the 28th of last month in which Japanese sailors robbed goods and injured people in Pudong, Huang Guangdou, the chief of the second section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, personally went to the Japanese consulate to lodge a verbal protest. At the same time, the bureau also investigated the details of the matter and reported it to the municipal government. According to the New Voice News Agency quoting Mayor Zhang yesterday, the municipal government formally submitted a written protest to the Japanese consulate general after receiving a detailed report and investigation of the matter. The content is divided into four points: (1) Please severely punish the sailors who landed and robbed goods and injured people. (2) Compensate the injured workers for medical expenses. (3) Make a formal apology. (4) Guarantee that similar unfortunate events will not happen again in the future. Mayor Zhang also said that although the goods robbed by the Japanese were found to be sold by Japanese merchants to Japanese merchants, if the inspectors made a mistake in inspection, they could only report to the Japanese authorities and negotiate with our side through legal procedures. They could never carry out forceful interference and allow Japanese soldiers to commit violence in our territory.

Business plummeted after being boycotted

Shanghai Inland River Vessels Fully Resumed Operations 146

Suspended during the flood season

Losses of more than 200,000

This year, major floods occurred in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. Starting in July, all inland river small vessels in the province were completely suspended. Shanghai's wheel companies have been out of business for three months, and the losses have been unprecedented. Afterwards, the ships were ordered to transport people from the disaster areas and were sent to Jiangxi inland to supply dispatches until now when they have resumed operations. The details are recorded as follows:

Inland River Fully Open: The first Shanghai inland river small vessel to resume navigation was the Shengou route, followed by the Shenhang route, the Shensu route, and the Shenchang routes. The last to sail was the Zhenyang route. Now the water in the canal has also receded sharply, and small vessels can be sailed to Zhenjiang and Jiangyin. The Shanghai Inland River Merchants Bureau has fully resumed operations of all Zhenyang Chengxi vessels. The bureau has a total of twenty-two routes, which are now all open.

Lake Route Dispute: The Huzhou route is the most competitive of the inland river small vessels in this port. There are six wheel companies running on the morning and evening shifts. In addition to the existing supply, Lixing Xinwheel Bureau has also added ships to the route. The Shenhu morning shift has already started sailing. Zhengchang and other six companies on the Huzhou line have unanimously opposed it and submitted a public petition to the Zhejiang Construction Office, requesting them to prevent and restrict the company, saying that they fear that there will be a wave of competition for navigation, such as the tragedy of the Shenchang class in the ninth year of the Republic of China when a ship was sunk and 27 lives were drowned, and the danger will reappear on the Shenhu line today. The Zhejiang Construction Office has already issued an order to investigate and stop this matter.

Yongan Resumes Operations: During the flood season, the small vessels of a certain company on the Shenhu route in this port destroyed the dike in Huzhou due to their huge horsepower. The Huzhou Farmers Association requested the provincial government to detain the vessel and discuss severe penalties. After more than two months of negotiations, the Huzhou class vessel has now fully resumed navigation, and a certain wheel company has also tried to mediate. According to reliable sources, the wheel company has admitted to paying a huge amount of money to settle the matter of destroying the dike, and the detained vessel will be released and returned on the same day. It can resume normal operations and navigation within this week.

Flood Losses: During the last major flood in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, the small vessels were suspended for a long time, resulting in huge losses. According to the Inland River Merchants Bureau, it lost a total of 30,000 taels of silver when the flood stopped navigation, excluding the branch offices in other places. The losses of other wheel companies totaled 200,000 yuan in Shanghai alone.

Sugar Industry Trade Association Meeting Record 148

Discussion of Bribery Case

The Sugar Industry Trade Association held its 18th Members' General Meeting at 1:00 PM on the 4th of this month, due to allegations of bribery against Chairman Zheng Zenan. Forty-two members, including Fang Cuihe, were present. He Wei was elected as chairman. The chairman first reported on: (1) the purpose of the meeting, (2) resolutions of the executive committee meetings on October 4th and 9th, (3) the Association's letter to the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association on the 3rd of this month, (4) the Municipal Chamber of Commerce's inquiry regarding the report in the newspaper on the 3rd of this month concerning the Association Chairman's alleged bribery through releasing goods. The following matters were then discussed: (1) Ratification of the 31st and 32nd executive committee meeting resolutions regarding the handling of the Yuan Yu Mao He case. Resolution: It was found that the Dongtang sugar sold by Yuan Yu was ordered between April and May. In July, the boycott occurred. Due to the deposit, the firm had to accept the warehouse warrants after the sugar arrived in Shanghai. In September, due to financial difficulties, over two hundred bags were sold. This was before the establishment of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association. Many businesses dealing in Japanese goods in this city were in similar situations, and their actions were somewhat excusable. Mao He only had suspicions of violating the previous Anti-Japanese Aid-the-Compatriots Association's announcement, which required that any detained enemy goods be handed over to the association for disposal. The nature of this case is different from the announcement, one being about past events and the other about suspicion. The executive committee's handling of Yuan Yu Mao He on the 9th does not seem to violate the previous Anti-Japanese Association's announcement and should be ratified. (2) Discussion of the allegations of bribery against Chairman Zheng and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce's letter of inquiry regarding this case. It was jointly discussed how to handle the case. Resolution: Yuan Yu donated 1,500 yuan to school funding, as stated by Yu Yizhai at the meeting. The firm made the donation voluntarily. Yu Yizhai also admitted that he gave 1,000 yuan to Zhu Anqing, as reported in the newspaper. He personally clarified this to Mr. Zhao at the Anti-Japanese Association at 5:00 PM on the 3rd of this month. Regarding the donation and bribery case, the truth is now clear. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce should be informed of the facts via letter, and a statement should be published in the newspaper.

Petition from China Merchants Electric Company 150

Regarding Employee Work Stoppage and Expulsion of Wu Quesheng

Employees of the Shanghai China Merchants Electric Company previously went on strike for three days, demanding that the company improve their treatment and expel Wu Quesheng, the head of the General Affairs Department. After the Municipal Party Department and others sent personnel to mediate, they resumed normal work. Now, the company believes that the right to employ personnel belongs to the company, so it rejected the employees' demands and dismissed Wu Quesheng. Furthermore, the company suffered losses of up to 4,600 yuan due to the employees' work stoppage. Yesterday, Lu Bohong, the manager of the company, submitted a petition to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, stating: Petition regarding a reply. The company received instruction No. 6640 from your bureau, which stated: In the matter of the company's employees requesting improved treatment, this bureau has decided to order compliance. According to reports, the employees expressed dissatisfaction and suddenly went on strike. A petition was submitted to the Municipal Government for review and judgment. Now, instruction No. 12464 from the Municipal Government was received, instructing on how to handle the matter, etc. Upon receipt, one copy of the original instruction was attached, and personnel from the Municipal Party Department were dispatched to persuade the employees to return to work. Please comply with the instruction. Upon receipt, the company found that the employees' demands for improved treatment were excessively demanding, even resorting to work stoppages to pressure the company. In law and in reason, there was no room for acceptance. However, your bureau repeatedly convened both parties for mediation, earnestly advocating for a peaceful resolution. The company appreciated your intention and reluctantly agreed to mediate, which can be considered a compromise and not a legal obligation to accept. Furthermore, the employees' act of posting slogans to expel Wu Quesheng, the head of the General Affairs Department, was utterly absurd. Wu Quesheng had resigned from the position of head of the General Affairs Department in May of this year due to illness and only served as the head of the Document Department. The manager and executive director had previously contacted your bureau and brought Wu, then the head of the department, along for note-taking. The employees then believed that Wu was obstructing their demands from being fully met and publicly advocated for his expulsion. They do not understand that the right to employ personnel belongs to the company and cannot be claimed by any employee. Therefore, when this matter was brought up for discussion at the board meeting on the 2nd of this month, it was unanimously deemed inappropriate and not approved. This must be stated first. Furthermore, the above-mentioned instruction stated that the company's employees violated the government's repeated orders by arbitrarily going on strike, which is even more inappropriate. This should be investigated and handled separately. The company suffered losses of 4,600 yuan due to the failure to issue tickets during the three-day work stoppage. How should the employees be held responsible for compensating for this loss, and how should they be punished according to the law for arbitrarily going on strike, clearly defying your instruction? Please provide clear instructions to maintain the rule of law. In addition, your bureau initially set the date for the company's reluctant agreement to increase salaries as January of next year. For this year, the company would follow your advice to raise subsidies to draw a clear line. However, the reported solution included the phrase "(to be implemented from October of the 20th year of the Republic)", which is inconsistent with the facts. In addition to having the manager represent the company and present the above-mentioned points in person, this petition is being submitted for clarification. Please review and approve as appropriate for public convenience. Respectfully submitted to Pan, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, and Lu Bohong, Manager of the Shanghai China Merchants Electric Company Limited. Enclosed: Municipal Government Instruction No. 12464. The petition and accompanying documents have been received and investigated by personnel. Further investigation revealed that paragraph one of the bureau's previously submitted report on the decision regarding the case (a 30% increase for those with monthly salaries of 36 yuan or more) should be cancelled. Please forward this to both labor and management for compliance. The company's employees violated the government's repeated orders by arbitrarily going on strike, which is highly inappropriate, especially during this critical period. This should be investigated and handled separately. Please forward this for notification. This instruction is hereby issued. Attachments are returned. October 30th, 20th year of the Republic of China. Mayor Zhang Qun.

Dafeng Textile Factory Work Stoppage Yesterday 151

All 600 workers at the Dafeng Textile Factory in Caojiadu, Shanghai West, automatically went on strike at 9:00 AM yesterday. After receiving the report, Party and government agencies immediately sent personnel to persuade them, investigate the truth, and handle the matter according to the facts. The details are reported below.

Reasons for the Work Stoppage: The working hours of all workers at the Dafeng Textile Factory were mediated by the Social Affairs Bureau and set at ten hours. Workers in the cloth weaving section claimed that Ye Qiuquan, an official of the factory, pressured workers and instigated his henchmen to force workers to sign agreements to restore the twelve and a half hour work day. Starting at 9:00 AM yesterday, they initiated the work stoppage. Workers in the dyeing and thread sections joined in. However, the factory stated that the factory law stipulates a maximum of ten hours and did not allow it, asking workers to sign voluntarily in order to report to Party and government agencies and request instructions.

Party and Government Persuasion: The 3rd District Dyeing Industry Workers' Union, upon seeing the workers' automatic work stoppage, sent Standing Director Li Junfeng and others to report to the Municipal Party Department and the Social Affairs Bureau. The factory also sent Lu Shiyi, director of the personnel department, to report. The Municipal Party Department, fearing the expansion of the dispute, sent Li Weixiong, together with Zhu Guilin of the Social Affairs Bureau, to persuade the workers to resume work first and await legal resolution, and to investigate the truth for handling according to the facts. The result was that all workers insisted on not resuming work unless Ye Qiuquan was dismissed. After repeated persuasion by union members, it is said that work may resume this morning. In general, this dispute is unlikely to escalate.

Invisible Resolution of British Public Bus Strike 153

Striking Workers Have Completely Lost Their Jobs

All 222 ticket sellers of the British Public Bus Company went on strike to demand better treatment and oppose the company's unwarranted dismissal of workers. Although Party and government agencies and Chinese directors intervened to mediate, the company's unyielding attitude and rejection of mediation have resulted in no solution for months. All the striking workers, with no avenue for appeal, have had to return their uniforms and badges, sever ties, and find other means of livelihood. The committee requesting reinstatement has been automatically and invisibly dissolved. The company has indicated that it will not rehire any of the striking workers, and has hired new workers. Although all bus lines have fully resumed operation, the new workers are not yet fully trained. All fares are temporarily uniform, with Route 1, 2, 9, and 10 selling for 16 cents and Route 5 selling for 10 cents. It is said that after the company made the ticket prices uniform, the number of passengers has actually increased, and the revenue has increased compared to before. Most of the uniforms of the former striking workers have already been returned.

Foreign Ships Volunteer to Transport Disaster Victims: Most of the flood victims from various provinces this year have sought refuge in Beijing and Shanghai. Therefore, it is proposed that the transportation group of the Disaster Relief Association also contact them to facilitate the procedures. After receiving the reply, the foreign affairs office submitted it to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for notification to the Beijing Municipal Government.
