Planting Rice on Seven Acres Yields Only Dozens of Catties

A Family of Eight Has No Way to Make a Living

This year, due to continuous autumn rains and tidal surges, the low-lying fields in Yangxing and Yuepu and other townships in Baoshan County have become swamps, and rice and cotton crops have failed, with no hope for the autumn harvest. The heads of various townships and districts have reported the famine situation to the county. Because it is currently the harvest season, the famine situation is becoming increasingly apparent. Those who sell rice are full of worry, sighing and complaining, and are largely unable to support themselves. A farmer named Sheng in Yangxing Township has 27 mu of grain land and a family of eight, who rely on farming for a living. This year, because all of his fields happened to be planted with rice (the fields in that area are planted with rice for two years out of every three, and with rice for one year), one mu of rice land was not planted. Unexpectedly, the harvest of cotton from these 27 mu of rice land was only dozens of catties (in previous years, it would have been dozens of dan). Therefore, Sheng was heartbroken to see this, filled with anger and worry about how his family of eight would survive in the future. Moreover, he thought that he had not planted rice, and there was no grain in his house, so he was extremely anxious. Therefore, the day before yesterday, after picking dozens of catties of white rice and taking it to the market for sale, he used the money he earned to buy two opium pipes, went home, secretly swallowed them, and lay down. Later, he groaned in pain as the poison took effect. His family did not know that he had committed suicide by swallowing opium. Unexpectedly, he was deeply poisoned, and soon died of suffocation. Only then did his family see the opium stains on his lips and realize that he had committed suicide due to the famine and the inability to maintain his family. The family, young and old, felt even more miserable.

Lawsuit for Letting Dogs Bite People 157

Calling a Doctor Results in Being Bitten by Dogs

The Owner Laughs Nearby

Bitten Until Gasping for Breath

Becomes a Lawsuit

Ma Wanyao, the son of the late famous throat doctor Ma Fengbo of Jiangwan, was recently sued in the First Special Court by Wu Boyou, a shopkeeper at Hengfeng Trading Company in Xiaobeimen Dongshunli, who hired lawyers He Sui and Wu Chengyu, accusing him of letting dogs bite people. The complaint stated that the plaintiff was a shopkeeper at Hengfeng Trading Company. On the evening of the 21st of this month (October) at 8:00 PM, because a partner was ill, he went to the clinic of the defendant, Dr. Ma Wanyao, to ask him to come for a consultation. As soon as he entered the door, the defendant released two vicious dogs that he kept, and they bit him fiercely. The defendant laughed nearby. When the plaintiff was injured and fell to the ground, gasping for breath, he ordered the dogs to stop biting. Although he was lucky to have survived, his head and feet were all seriously injured. He asked a surgeon for an examination, who said that it would be difficult to recover completely in a short time and that he might become disabled. He submitted a report to the Procuratorate of the Court on the 22nd, which proved that the injury was real. The defendant has violated Article 293, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law, and is also filing a civil suit, requesting a judgment ordering compensation for medical expenses of 7,700 yuan and other losses of 300 yuan. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Shen Dumu presided over the hearing. The defendant also hired lawyer Wen Chao to appear in court, stating that the main subject of the plaintiff's complaint was mistaken, because the defendant, Ma Wanyao, is the son of Ma Fengbo, who died many years ago. At the time, the plaintiff wanted to hire Ma Fengbo. Therefore, Ma Fengbo's grandson, Ma Bosun (i.e., Ma Wanyao's nephew), responded to the consultation, and the dogs were also kept by Bosun. Therefore, the main subject of the plaintiff's complaint is mistaken and should be rejected. The plaintiff's lawyer then stated that the doctor the plaintiff wanted to hire was Ma Fengbo. Now that Fengbo is said to have died many years ago, it is difficult to prove at the time whether the dogs were kept by Ma Wanyao or Ma Bosun, and afterwards, the plaintiff sent a letter to Ma Fengbo, which was received by Ma Wanyao with a seal. Therefore, Wanyao and Bosun should be sued together. Judge Shen ordered the plaintiff's lawyer to file a corrected statement and reschedule the hearing.

Hangzhou Kidnapper Wu Tianbao Captured 158

Confesses to Shooting Jiang Zhongyun

Accomplice Sun Naitai and Others Captured

On the 24th of last month, Jiang Zhongyun, a detective chief of the Hangzhou County Public Security Bureau, came to Shanghai on a mission to arrest Wu Tianbao, the ringleader of a series of major kidnapping and robbery cases in Hangzhou. He was ambushed in a den at No. 1 Beidiao Fang, Beidiaoao Road, in the French Concession. The bandit had been aware in advance and ambushed next to the escalator on the upper floor. Shooting from above, he seriously injured Detective Jiang and French Concession detective Ni Jinrong and detective Wang Jinyu. Wu escaped from the scene, and Detective Jiang died in the line of duty. The details have been reported in this newspaper. Since the incident, the French Concession authorities have paid extraordinary attention and have repeatedly ordered their subordinates to intensify their efforts to solve the case and bring the notorious thief Wu Tianbao to justice in the shortest possible time for severe punishment. Until 8:00 PM last night, Jin Jiu, inspector general of the special agency of the French Concession Police Department, received a confidential report stating that Wu was hiding during the day and active at night, and his whereabouts were extremely secretive, but every night after 9:00 PM, he would go to Sun Naitai's, a fellow from Shaoxing, on the second floor of No. 9 Taiheli, Baierbu Road, for secret talks. He requested that detectives be dispatched to arrest him as soon as possible. Upon hearing the report, Inspector General Jin immediately led a full team of detectives, including detective Li Yaolong, deputy detective Mao Jingen, Qian Yumin, Zhang Ziying, and detective Qin Youyu, disguised themselves and went to the vicinity of the police kiosk to wait. At 9:10 PM, Wu arrived, looking around suspiciously, and went into No. 9. The detectives surrounded the area and stormed into the house, capturing the bandit on the spot and seizing a loaded pistol with seven bullets, along with his accomplice Sun Naitai and four other suspects. They were all detained in the police station. After a preliminary interrogation by the police chief, Wu, 31 years old, from Shaoxing, confessed to the previous shooting and resistance to arrest. The police chief ordered him to be detained pending extradition to the court for severe punishment.

Resisting Foreign Goods: Chinese Organize the Improved Native Cloth Association 159

Since the Chinese people severed economic ties with Japan, various industries have been thinking about improving domestic products to replace Japanese goods. Xu Ji'an and Wang Shipeng, members of the Shanghai Dye Association, observed that the native cloth produced in Jiangyin, a city in China, has always been very fine. Last month, they sent people to Jiangyin to investigate and find ways to improve, promote, and popularize it. They also organized the Shanghai Improved Native Cloth Promotion Association in order to promote it as much as possible.

Embezzling More Than 100,000 Yuan Through Marking 160

Collusion From Inside and Out

The Shop Owner Entrusted the Wrong Person

Fu Boliang from Shaoxing, an employee of the Shaoxing Tiancheng Silver Building, was recently sent to Shanghai by his employer to serve as the fully empowered representative of the silver building for marking gold purchases and sales. Recently, the gold market has soared, and Tiancheng has collected a large amount of cash and sent it to Shanghai, asking Fu to sell it. Unexpectedly, Fu colluded with Zhu Wenbo, the manager of the silver building, and after selling the cash, did not send all of the money to Tiancheng, embezzling as much as 150,000 taels. Recently, shareholder Li Yongquan discovered this and reported it to the Shaoxing Local Court. After investigation, the prosecutor found it to be true and filed a public prosecution, detaining Zhu Wenbo first. At the same time, Li Yongquan came to Shanghai to visit Fu. The day before yesterday, Li learned that Fu was hiding in Room 55, Baohe Hotel, Ziyoufang, Guangdong Road, and reported it to the Lao Zha Police Station. Detective Chen Yonggui was ordered to arrest Fu. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Criminal Court of the First Special Court. According to Ru Baozhi, the police lawyer, the plaintiff in this case has already filed a lawsuit with the official court, so Fu Boliang should be transferred to Shaoxing for trial. However, the Shaoxing Local Court did not send anyone to receive him today, so he requested a postponement of one week. Li Yongquan then complained about the situation. Fu Boliang also confessed to embezzling more than 100,000 yuan. Judge Zhou Hanting verified the confession and ordered that the case be rescheduled for one week for further verification.

Truth of Mercury in Noodles Case Still Unclear 161

No Sales Found in Nearby Drugstores

Wu Yantian Is Proceeding with Divorce

Wu Yantian, a coppersmith from Anhui residing at No. 316 Ruijin Road, reported that at noon on the 27th of last month, his wife, Bian, put mercury in noodles with the intention of poisoning him. Wu discovered this and reported it to the Harbin Police Station, which dispatched Peng Yushan to arrest Bian and escort her to the Special District Court for questioning. This has already been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiao Xiefen presided over the investigation in the Third Criminal Court. According to Zhang Tianyin, the police lawyer, during the postponement, the police ordered detectives to investigate drugstores in the vicinity of the victim's residence to see if anyone had purchased mercury that morning. All said that they had not sold this kind of drug in several months. The defendant also firmly denied this in the police station. The doctor at the Public Works Bureau Hospital examined the bottom of the noodle bowl eaten by the victim and found mercury, which was taken out and placed in a small glass bottle, weighing five li. The bottle was presented for inspection. However, the nature of this material cannot be known in advance by non-experts. At the time, there were four bowls of noodles cooked, but only the victim's bowl had mercury at the bottom. Moreover, that morning, the victim intended to give his eleven-year-old daughter to another family as a child bride, but the defendant did not agree, leading to a dispute and the poisoning. Please investigate strictly. According to Wu Yantian, that morning, he was sleeping upstairs on the third floor and told Bian to bring the noodles upstairs for him to eat alone. Afterwards, he found this poisonous substance at the bottom of the bowl. He had never heard of Bian having any irregular behavior and hired a lawyer to defend him. In addition to punishing Bian, he also filed a divorce suit. When questioned, Wu Bian firmly denied it and also hired a lawyer to defend her. Judge Xiao ordered a date for sentencing. When she saw her eleven-year-old daughter standing next to her father wearing an old silk cheongsam, she demanded that the daughter go to prison with her, saying that the silk clothes worn by the daughter were not from her family, but had been sold by her father to others. She cried loudly. Afterwards, the court ordered police detectives to investigate. If the plaintiff had sold his daughter, he would be arrested immediately. Bian then stopped crying and returned to temporary detention.

Kidnapped Victim Rescued in Songjiang 162

Fan Guozhong Rescues Han Quanfa

Han Liansheng, a farmer from Hanjiazhai, Liuzao, Dazhangjing, Songjiang, has dozens of mu of thin land, which is enough for food and clothing. He has only one son, named Han Quanfa, who is ten years old and is very fond of him. In the middle of last month, a gang of bandits came to his house and kidnapped Quanfa. Han immediately reported it to the Land and Water Public Security Bureau for a thorough investigation. It has now been learned that the kidnapped victim and the kidnappers are hiding in a house at No. 1041 Yangshupu in Shanghai. The captain immediately led police detectives to Shanghai and, in cooperation with the detectives, secretly went to the house and rescued the kidnapped victim Han Quanfa. However, the kidnappers were well-informed and had already fled. It was found that the kidnapped victim had been hiding in the bandits' den for nearly a month and was mentally exhausted. Yesterday, Captain Fan took the kidnapped victim on the Shanghai-Hangzhou express train and returned to the Zhujing team headquarters for his family to pick him up. At the same time, he ordered detectives to track down the kidnappers and bring them to justice according to law.

Kidnapper Xu A'gen Extradited to Shanghai 163

Xu A'gen, a tea servant in the Southeast Hotel in Caishi Street and a pimp in the prostitute house, kidnapped the child Wang Tongsheng from Huangdai, Suzhou, and was caught on the train. He has been taken into custody by the Local Court. Xu hired a gasoline boat as the helmsman to kidnap the child. He secretly reported it to the Suzhou Public Security Bureau, so Xu was arrested. The day before yesterday, the Local Court sent bailiffs Zou Zhendong and Hu Xianglin to Suzhou to extradite him to Shanghai for trial.

Trial of a Large Group of Notorious Robbers 164

The Trial of Shen Shouying and Five Others Begins

Remaining Notorious Robbers to be Interrogated Later

Last month, the robber Ji Dahua gathered Yu Hengdao and Du Qizhi, armed them, and drove a stolen car to rob a certain family in the French Concession's Kangti Road, Quadali. They happened upon a special investigation unit of the French police, who were on patrol, so they did not dare proceed with the robbery. Yu and Du, carrying guns, fled back to the Huabin Hotel in Hongyunfang. Ji parked the car by the roadside and was discovered by investigators and arrested. Yu and Du were also apprehended, and individuals related to the case, including Hu Naiguang, Yu Bulou, and Qian Guangshu, were subsequently arrested. Suspicious individuals, including Shen Shouying, Chen Jinshan, Shan Yaonan, Zhang Fenglou, Dong Linshan, and Xu Lianyuan, a total of twelve people, were searched, yielding two handguns, bullet casings, and other items. It was also discovered that Ji, Yu, and Du had successively robbed the Yuchang shop at No. 38, Baoxingli, No. 33, and the Yunnan woman Chen Wangshi at No. 101 Sapo Race Road, taking their belongings. Qian Guangshu was linked to the case where Wu Tingfang, the bookkeeper of the Ruikang Paint Shop, jumped from a building and died. They were handed over to the Second Special Court's Criminal Division for interrogation. Due to the police investigation being incomplete, the interrogation was postponed. Yesterday, the due date arrived. At 2 PM, Judge Ge Zhitan took his seat in Criminal Court One for the continued interrogation. First, the police lawyer Fei Xizhen stated that, since the postponement, the police had discovered that Ji Wenhua, Du Qizhi, Yu Hengdao, Hu Naiguang, Yu Bulou, and Qian Guangshu were involved in the case and had conspired with the fugitive Mao Platoon Leader in a Nanjing hotel to plan three robberies. The police were prosecuting them for robbery. The remaining six defendants were not involved in the case, and the police requested instructions. Immediately thereafter, Shi Changfu, representing Wang Licai of No. 33 Baoxingli, Li Bingzhang, representing Liu Yangsan of the Yuchang shop at No. 38, and Chen Wangshi, the three victims, described the circumstances of the robberies. Chen Wangshi identified the defendant Yu Hengdao as having threatened her on the stairs with a gun at the time of the robbery. When Ji Wenhua was questioned, he confessed that the fugitive Mao Platoon Leader was the mastermind and that he, Yu Hengdao, Du Qizhi, and others had gone to commit robberies, but that he had not personally robbed anyone, only received money afterwards. He also stated that on the night of his arrest, they had planned to rob a "huahui" (flower club) telephone booth. Yu and Du confessed to having robbed the three victims. Hu Naiguang stated that the car used by Ji was initially purchased by a civilian for 300 yuan. However, because he could not obtain a license, he asked Ji to sell it for 400 yuan. He went to the Huabin Hotel to find Ji to collect the car price but did not see Yu and Du. They handed him a paper package, which he later realized contained a handgun, which he then discarded near the pit on the fourth floor of the hotel. He claimed no knowledge of the robbery. Yu Bulou stated that he had been to the Nanjing hotel but did not know of any discussions about robbery. Qian Guangshu confessed that on May 26th, Xue Xing invited him to No. 2, Sichengli, to discuss kidnapping and showed him a "ticket." He did not participate in the kidnapping, which was carried out by Xue and five other unknown individuals. On June 15th, the hostage jumped from a building and died. They were eating when the incident occurred and fled immediately. On September 14th, Yu Hengdao, Du Qizhi, and others discussed robbery in a Nanjing hotel. He provided the handgun, which he borrowed from Sister Zhu and returned to her after the robbery. He received eight yuan as his share afterwards. When questioned, Shen Shouying and the other six defendants all stated that they were completely unaware of the robbery and had been wrongly arrested, requesting investigation. Judge Ge, after reviewing the confessions, acquitted Shen Shouying, Chen Jinshan, Shan Yaonan, Zhang Fenglou, Dong Linshan, and Xu Lianyuan, and ordered their immediate release. The remaining six defendants were ordered to be detained in the detention center, and the continued interrogation was scheduled for November 14th, with assigned defense lawyers.

Public Steersman Sheng's Sandboat Capsized in a Hurricane 165

The Shandong Kui Sheng He sandboat, with Public Steersman Sheng on board, recently loaded more than 40,000 taels of salted hairtail and northern goods in Lushun and sailed to Shanghai to sell. On the 27th of last month, the boat was sailing in the northeastern waters of Tongshan when it suddenly encountered a hurricane. They steered toward the coast to seek shelter, but accidentally struck a reef and became stuck. The boat was immediately flooded. The boat owner, Jiang Yonghe, seeing the boat gradually sinking, instructed his crew to raise a distress flag and ring a gong for help. Unfortunately, the wind and waves were too strong, and no ships passed by to rescue them. The crew of thirty-three men were terrified. They lowered a sampan to escape, but the boat was too small for so many people. A sudden gust of wind capsized the sampan. The crew members on the boat saw the sampan capsize and the crew members floating in the sea. Unable to save them, they threw ropes into the sea, rescuing three people. Eleven crew members remained on the boat. The following morning, at dawn, some crew clung to the boat's planks and called for help as they drifted with the waves, but no ships came. Boat owner Jiang Yonghe and two crew members grabbed onto the top of the mast and waited for rescue. In the afternoon, the Jingyun steamship passed by and saw them. It dropped anchor, lowered a small boat, and rescued Jiang and the two crew members, providing them with clothes to change. The ship sailed past Haimen, dropped Jiang and the two off at the dock, and gave them two dollars each to take a boat to Shanghai. Jiang and the two crew members took the Jufeng Company's boat and arrived in Shanghai yesterday, reporting the incident to the sales agent and informing the Shandong company. It is reported that when the boat sank, eight crew members clung to the planks and drifted in the ocean, it is unknown whether they were rescued. Over twenty crew members on the poop deck perished, sinking into the sea before their eyes.

Yuan Ludeng, a Ningbo merchant in Shanghai, celebrated the 162nd birthdays of his respected father, Mr. Xieyuan, and his mother, Madam Hu, this year. Coinciding with widespread floods, the charitable Yuan family donated over 30,000 yuan in congratulatory gifts from relatives and friends to aid disaster relief, benefiting many victims. The following day, Yuan held a birthday celebration for his parents and a thank-you event for relatives and friends, with another grand theater performance. Many Chinese and foreign guests offered congratulations. Prominent figures from the party and government, such as Chairman Chiang, Minister Kong, and Minister Wang, all sent congratulatory gifts. Important figures from the local military, political, business, academic circles, and the Western directors of the Municipal Council all personally offered congratulations.

Detective Team Discovers a Large Flower Gambling Den 167

Commissioner Chen of the Municipal Public Security Bureau received a tip-off the other day, stating that a large-scale "huahui" (flower gambling) den was located on the upper floor of No. 34 Laoguangdong Street, Gaochang Temple, in the South City, luring people to gamble large sums of money daily, severely harming society. He requested that officers be dispatched quickly to arrest them and restore peace to the area. Upon receiving the report, Commissioner Chen secretly instructed Detective Captain Lu Ying to handle the matter properly. Yesterday, Captain Lu secretly dispatched squad leader Qi Haitian, along with detectives Wu Zuorong and Zhang Quanzhou, together with Inspector Tang from the Inspectorate, to conduct a raid at the address. They arrested the gambling boss Chen Hengxia, the woman Chen Yu, and the accomplice Qin Fu, seizing many gambling slips. After a preliminary interrogation by Captain Lu, they confessed to privately setting up a gambling den and luring people to gamble. Report on the Charitable Deeds of the Tongren Fuyuan Hall 169

Report on the charitable deeds carried out by the Shanghai Charity Organization Tongren Fuyuan Hall in October: (1) Rice rations were given to 350 widows, 395 disabled people, 100 poor people, and 104 security personnel (one yuan each). 50 orphans received support (8 jiao each), totaling 953 yuan. (2) Coffins were provided: 125 large and 106 small coffins to the Xin Puyu Hall, 38 large coffins to the Jiangsu Second Prison, 6 large coffins to the Disaster Relief Shelter Sub-Division (all collected by the Pushan Villa for burial), 21 small coffins (collected by the Hall's workers for burial), 32 large and 78 small coffins were distributed to hospitals and at the door, 50 bone boxes for tomb relocation on Kang Nao Road in the Public Concession, 62 large and 71 small coffins to the Tongren Fuyuan Sub-Hall, and 12 large and 142 small coffins to the Tongren Fuyuan Rescue Bureau, totaling 750 coffins and bone boxes. (3) Burial services were provided: 162 large and 300 small coffins by the Tongren Fuyuan Hall, 70 large and 276 small coffins by the Tongren Fuyuan Sub-Hall, 38 large and 173 small coffins by the Tongren Fuyuan Rescue Bureau, and 270 small coffins in the Qichang Stack area of Pudong, from Yangjing Town in the east to Shibajian in the west, from Tangqiao in the south to the Huangpu in the north, totaling 1289 large and small coffins. Apart from the Qichang Stack area, where burials were done on the spot, the remains were moved to the Tangwan Township cemetery for burial. (4) Medical supplies were distributed to 812 patients. The list was compiled and submitted to the Social Bureau for record-keeping by Qin Yanqi and Zhu Qingsheng, the directors of the Hall.

Supplement Three of the Shanghai Financial History Published 171

The revised and updated Shanghai Financial History, compiled by Xu Jiqing of Yongjia, has been popular at home and abroad since its publication and has long been known as the "Southern Dipper" of the financial world. Supplements One and Two were added last year, detailing the financial situation of 1928 and 1929, and were well-received by readers. To supplement the financial data for 1930, Xu has compiled "Supplement Three," which specifically publishes the business reports of Chinese and foreign banks, trust companies, savings societies, and the survey reports of various money shops in Shanghai in 1930. The content is rich and more complete than before. The book has been published and contains over 160 pages, selling for 2 jiao per copy. It is sold at the Shanghai Commercial Press and the Bank Weekly. There are few original copies of the Financial History left, selling for 1.50 yuan each. Supplements One and Two are still included with the original copy without additional charge.

The autumn champagne tickets for the members of the Shanghai Race Club at the Race Course Road in this city were drawn on November 3rd at 7 PM in public due to the change of regulations for the Shanghai Race Club champagne tickets. Opening of Lehua Hosiery Factory Yesterday 184

The Lehua Hosiery Factory on Xiaodongmennei Main Street opened yesterday amidst the sound of drums. The number of customers in the morning and afternoon was extremely crowded. Many celebrities in the hosiery industry went to visit and congratulate. Throughout the day, the "Green Tree" brand silk thread wool socks were the best-selling. The total income was around 10,000.

Free Distribution of Common Knowledge of Children's Diseases 185

"Common Knowledge of Children's Diseases" written by Dr. Zhang Juying comprehensively describes the general symptoms, etiology, treatment, medication, suitable food, and nursing methods for common childhood illnesses. Special attention is given to diseases unique to children, such as measles, smallpox, and infantile convulsion. It also discusses how to prevent illness and nurture children. It is recommended that families with children purchase a copy for reference. To commemorate his relocation, Dr. Zhang is offering free copies starting from October, but only to those who personally request them in this city. Those requesting by mail within this city must attach two cents for postage, and those outside the city must attach twenty cents. Dr. Zhang's current residence is No. 9, Beilong, Junyi Lane, Yijie Road.

Case of Sanyi Company, a Member of the Color Printing Industry 186

The Shanghai Color Printing Trade Association previously held an extraordinary meeting of member representatives and resolved to expel Sanyi Printing Company from membership. It is reported that Sanyi Company has expressed dissatisfaction with this decision and has sent a letter to the association requesting reconsideration, as well as a letter to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce requesting intervention.

Dahua Company's Flying Horse Brand Red Lead Powder 187

Dahua Red Lead Powder Company has specially hired expert technicians to produce a type of red lead powder using scientific methods. When applied to ironware, it can prevent rust and can also be used for dyeing paper, dyeing thread, and scraping paint. Many famous domestic factories and railways have adopted it. The company is located at No. 30, Wangjiazhai, Wengjiasha, behind the Artillery Factory in Gaichang Temple, Nanshi.

News from Various Trade Unions 188

The Pharmaceutical Workers' Union held its eighth council meeting yesterday. Chairman Zhao Zhenhui presided over the meeting in due form and reported (omitted). The meeting discussed various cases: (1) The proposal from Zhang Henian, Baokang, and other three stores regarding the self-government regulations for union members was submitted for review and approval. It was resolved to be handled by the training and organization departments. (2), (4) Omitted. (5) Shao Chunhua, a cadre of the Second District Branch, requested resignation due to old age. It was resolved to instruct the store's group to elect a capable replacement from among the group leaders. (6) Secret. (7) Regarding the current meeting of various trade unions to prevent troublemakers from taking advantage of the situation and the establishment of a liaison office for prevention, it was resolved to nominate Fang Qingjian and Zhao Zhenhui to participate. (8) Omitted. (9) Regarding whether to appoint a person to manage the newly introduced monthly fee stamps, it was resolved to appoint Feng Xinggeng. (10) Regarding whether the union should periodically convene a citywide meeting of group leaders to discuss various issues, it was resolved to convene on the 12th of this month at 1 PM and nominate Zhao Zhenhui, Fang Qingjian, and Fang Qinghe as the presidium. (11) The Lianyi Society resolved to transfer various unemployment registration cases to the union for ratification. It was resolved to approve them. (12) The supervisory committee resolved that Lianyi Society had not received 18 society certificates and requested an extension of three days. It was resolved that this case conflicted slightly with the union's previous proposal and would be reserved for reconsideration at the next joint meeting of the council. The cases of Jia Jiaxiang and Wu Deshun, who requested issuance within the deadline, would be handled together.

The Coal and Firewood Workers' Preparatory Committee held its tenth standing committee meeting the day before yesterday. Chairman Hu Chuzhao recorded the minutes. Yao Suikai presided over the meeting in due form. The chairman reported (omitted). Matters discussed: (1) Regarding how to handle member registration, it was resolved to dispatch personnel from November 5th to copy the lists separately. Zheng Xiaotang and Chen Baoqing would be responsible for the New Gate and Zhabei areas, while Xie Baoxing and Zhou Shanben would be responsible for the Nanshi and Hongkou areas. The work must be completed within one week and reported back. (2) A letter of introduction from Zhao Erchang of the party headquarters recommending Chen Pengnian to work at the committee was approved. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

The Fourth District Sanitation Workers' Union held its eleventh council meeting the day before yesterday. Chairman Zhu Shousheng reported on the following matters: (1) Regarding the dispute between Chen and Cao at the original site of Tianshengtang on Hongxing Road, it was resolved that the union, in order to enforce discipline, would still send personnel to work as previously agreed and would not tolerate any disobedience. (2) Regarding how to rectify the fact that a few union officials often neglect their duties, it was resolved that each should fulfill their duties and those who disobey would be dealt with in accordance with the regulations and reported to the higher authorities for approval. (3) It was resolved that the entire union should assist union officials who encounter disputes while performing their duties to show solidarity. (4) Regarding the disputes caused by workers competing for land when building houses on vacant land, it was resolved to act in accordance with the employer's wishes. The rest omitted.

Weather Report 189

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the weather was cloudy and cold, with strong seasonal winds coming from the north to northeast across the country's coast. There was a cyclone in southern Japan, and the weather was bad. Also, in the 24 hours before 3 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 66.4 and the lowest was 50.4. On the same day last year, the highest was 52.7 and the lowest was 32.9.

Reader's Letter 190

A Certain Gentleman's Message (Reporting a Large Shipment of Japanese Goods Entering Jiujiang)

The Jiujiang Anti-Japanese Association seized a large batch of Japanese textiles on the Taikoo Wharf yesterday. Upon discovery, the goods were immediately detained pending resolution. It was found that these Japanese goods were worth over 10,000 taels of silver and belonged to four well-known cloth stores in this city. The store owners or their managers are all prominent figures in the local business community. In the face of national crisis, every citizen should be motivated by conscience to sever economic ties with Japan and urge them to reflect. However, these gentlemen have dared to disregard the disapproval of the entire nation and have been blinded by profit, violating the patriotic movement and acting shamelessly and unconscionably. Furthermore, it is reported that this batch of Japanese goods used the trademarks of a certain British brand and changed the names one by one. At first glance, they appear to be Western goods, making it difficult for buyers to identify them. Their intentions can be described as cunning. Considering that the import and export of goods and the loading and unloading of ships cannot be done without the help of workers, such a large batch of enemy goods was imported into the interior, yet the Shanghai Anti-Japanese Association was deceived and failed to discover it. If merchants everywhere imitate the above method of disguising and distributing goods, they will still flood the market. If so, the effectiveness of our boycott will only be equal to zero. I humbly submit what I have heard with a clear conscience. In addition to writing directly to the Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association requesting that they strengthen their surveillance and prevent the source, I respectfully request that your newspaper publish this letter so that the anti-Japanese authorities in various places will pay attention to it. I am eagerly awaiting it.

Communication Stamp 191

Affix this stamp when communicating

Include stamps of appropriate value with the letter

To the Esteemed Editor:

Today, I saw a report stating that Jiading party members Lu Guanqün et al. sent a telegram regarding peace and unity. The last paragraph mentions "Lu Changlin and Sun Zongbing" and other party members from Songjiang County. The wording expresses dissatisfaction with Mr. Hu Hanmin's attitude. I had no prior knowledge of this telegram, and I am not acquainted with the lead signatory, Comrade Lu Guanqün. Most strangely, Songjiang County party member Sun Zongbing currently works at the Xiamen Radio Station, and his party membership has long been transferred. It is hateful that names are being borrowed to publish opinions. In addition to writing to Comrade Lu Guanqün, I am also writing to your newspaper requesting that this letter be published promptly in the "Letters to the Editor" section to clarify the truth and stop the speculation. Your assistance will be greatly appreciated. Wishing you peace, Lu Changlin, Executive Committee Member of Songjiang County. November 4th.

Youth Garden

The First Time 192

— Cheng

"I am very happy. Several of your classmates in your grade have made very rapid progress in English. I know this is the result of your efforts. Therefore, there is really no need to worry about classmates whose English is not very good. You just need to work harder. There is absolutely nothing difficult in the world, and there is no effort that goes unrewarded." Mr. Wang, the English teacher, said happily, standing on the right side of the podium. He was very young, very handsome, and it was said that he had never been married. We admired him very much and respected him for his talent and appearance.

After he finished speaking, the classroom was particularly quiet. Everyone lowered their heads, looking at the books as if very attentively. Qi, who was sitting on my left, lowered her head even lower than the other students, and a faint blush appeared on her fair face. At that time, I knew that Qi was one of those the teacher was referring to when he said, "English is improving very quickly," because her progress was very rapid. Recently, she could almost be said to be the best in English in the whole grade.

Two weeks later, Mr. Wang gave a topic in English composition class, saying, "Write a letter to your friend." After the teacher wrote the topic, he turned around and glanced at Qi with a happy smile, and then said, "Today's topic is very easy, right?" Many students happily answered, "It's easy. It's best to give more topics like this in the future, because the scope is large and we can easily develop our ideas." The teacher's smiling face seemed even happier at this time.

Two days later, the teacher had finished grading our papers and returned them to us. As usual, the students asked, "Whose English composition is the best?" They all hoped that their English composition would improve, so they always asked the best English composition students to take a look. The teacher's attitude did not seem as calm as usual, but after a while, he said very calmly, "That topic was easy, almost everyone did well. Now, I'll tell you, if you want to improve your English quickly, you should pay attention to the textbooks I teach, and you should also study the English books in the library more. Are there any of you who often go to the library? The books in the library are very good teachers for you and me. After class, you should go there."

After the English class, we didn't have any more classes, so a very loud voice said, "Who's going to the library? Those who are going, come with me quickly!" Many students also shouted back loudly, "Going, going!" and then hopped out of the classroom.

The teacher's words didn't seem to have any possible doubts, but the nervous me always felt that the teacher was a little different from usual, and Qi, who was sitting on my left, also made me feel that she was a little special.

Usually, when the teacher returned our English composition notebooks, Qi would always ask me, "What's your score?" and ask me to borrow my paper to take a look. But this time, when she got the paper, she opened it, glanced at it quickly, and then closed it, put it in the desk, and silently read the textbook.

Seeing her attitude, I suspected that she had either gotten a very good score or a very bad score. But after thinking for a while and observing her expression, I thought Qi would definitely not get a very bad score, because she had improved a lot this semester. Before she improved, her English composition was also within the top ten or so. So I thought she must have gotten a very good score... But after thinking about it, it didn't seem right. The time before last, before the teacher said that Qi was the best, she had happily put her paper in front of me and said with a smile, "Ninety-eight points, ninety-eight points!"

I spent the whole class in conjecture and curiosity. After the English class, the students of the grade all walked out of the classroom, except for me, Qi, and Wang and Zhang, who were writing love letters in the row farthest from me.

I noticed that Qi was a little special, so I gently asked her to see her English composition notebook. At the same time, I also gave her my English composition notebook.

Page 20

"Oh, it's nothing good, don't borrow it to take a look." Qi's expression seemed to be begging me, but when I saw the shallow smile on her face, her undisguised happy smile, I felt even more curious and even more inexplicable. So I continued, insisting on seeing her English composition notebook.

"Qi, to be honest with you, you are very different today than other days. If you have any secrets... any things that you don't want your classmates to know, you can tell me. I will definitely not tell anyone. Don't you believe that I am your best friend?" I said softly in her ear.

"There is nothing that I don't want my classmates to know about me. However, you know that the classmates' mouths are often idle, and they are usually good at exaggeration. If they know about me and Mr. Wang, wouldn't it be very inconvenient for Mr. Wang?" Qi said in a low voice with a blushing face, as she opened her English composition notebook for me to see.

"Oh, what a..." In Qi's English composition notebook, there was a letter written by Mr. Wang to Qi, with the opening salutation written as "My dear Qi." As soon as I saw it, I shouted out loudly unconsciously, but immediately stopped, when I realized that I was shouting loudly.

Wang and Zhang, who were writing love letters, turned around and glanced at us, asked "What's the matter?" and then continued to immerse themselves in writing love letters.

"Really, I feel really inexplicable. That day, the teacher gave the topic 'Write a letter to your friend,' and I vaguely wrote this love letter. That annoying Mr. Wang, I don't know why, even wrote me back a letter," Qi said as if calling out, as I looked at their love letter.

"No, I think Mr. Wang wrote it vaguely just like you. The deeper the love, the more vague the writing. So, in short, it is your love at work. Look, Wang and Zhang don't know what we are talking about, because they are vaguely intoxicated in their love," I said, pointing at Wang and Zhang. "You are terrible," Qi said with a smile as she hit me on my left shoulder.

Art World

Recent Irish Literary Scene 193

— Cong Ren

Mr. J.P. McGinley said at a meeting of the Irish Library Association, "If I had the power of a dictator, I would throw most of the books into the sea. Nine-tenths of the books selected for libraries represent the minds, interests, actions, and moral standards of the British. Sound films and radio are also opposed to our Irish education, because they come to our Irish ranks to spread their British and American ideas. These sound films and radio must be destroyed or monitored." From this, we can see how thorough the Irish people's spirit of nationalism is. In the field of literature and art, we can understand this situation even more clearly. Denis Johnstone's expressionist play "The Old Lady Says No" has made a comeback at the Gate Theatre, and his "Dublin Review" and the unstoppable, persevering Oliver St. John Gogarty's lyrics written on it were also performed in "Easter." When the two Russian films "Storm Over Asia" and "The End of St. Petersburg" were screened, more than six thousand people went to see them. Last autumn, the Peacock Theatre also screened an Irish "Amorous" film. Mr. Shaw's recent attempt to use new drama form, "Words Upon the Window Pane", was also performed at the Abbey Theatre. The Gate Theatre retaliated against the Abbey Theatre with the play "Back to Methuselah," calling the theatre full, and the Abbey Theatre retaliated against the Gate Theatre with Lennox Robinson's modernized translation of "The Critic." Robinson got the opportunity to ridicule Dublin's publishing, criticism, and intellectual circles for "The Critic." Mr. Sam Beekett, who is currently a French lecturer at Trinity College, has also written a study of Proust. A very modern bookstore has recently opened on Tavern Street.

The Publication Examination Bureau is also very diligent in promoting the moral well-being of Irish readers. "New Leader" was recently banned from publication for publishing an advertisement for birth control. Novels by Aldous Huxley, Somsrest Maugham, Liam O'Flaherty, and Lewis Sinclair have also been banned, because "their overall trend is obscene. But elsewhere, books on birth control must be freely advertised under the fierce light of inspection. Marie Stopes, Margaret Sanger, and even Russell are regarded as damaging to public morals. Only Eliner Glyn, Ethel M. Dnll, and Margaret Reterson are left to do this good work.

Also, Peader O'Donnell recently changed the name of his "The Knife" to "There Will Be Fighting" and published it in the United States. O'Donnell can be regarded as the greatest Irish writer of the last decade, but he is still relatively unknown among the intellectual circles in Dublin. This is mostly because he does not show his personality in "First Nights" and "The Sunday Evening Post." They really only read his books in "The Sunday Observer", which other people consider to be a good British review. But those who only knew about Joyce ten years after the world discovered Joyce are not expected to know about O'Donnell now. O'Donnell has published four novels, which describe the lives of farmers and their various aspects of national struggle. "Storm" was probably published ten years ago and is now out of print. This novel showed his hopes for success. The first few chapters of the book describe the storm along the coast of Donegal, which is beautifully written, but other than that, there is nothing remarkable about it. In 1925, he gave the manuscript of another novel to O'Flaherty. O'Flaherty read it once, sealed it in an envelope, and sent it to his own publisher, Johnathan Capo. Soon, "Islander" was published in England, and critics said that it was a masterpiece describing peasant life. Later, the book was renamed "The Way it Was with Them" and appeared in the United States. In 1927, while he was writing, he suddenly received the news that the Sullivan family of Adrigoolc had starved to death. As a result, he wrote his third novel, "Adrigoolc," in anger and pity. This book is still considered his most perfect work. His fourth novel, "The Knife," shows great progress in technique. However, O'Donnell's best works have not yet come. He is only thirty-five years old now. Although many years of fierce struggle, forty-one days of hunger strike, and constant revolutionary activities have left their marks on his body, he is still surprisingly lively. His upcoming novel is the last volume of a set that combines with the previous four books. After this book is written, he will start his new work from a larger perspective... a "History of Ireland after 1830" similar to Krupotkin's "History of the French Revolution".

Now O'Donnell is very free. What I mean is that he has not been arrested by the police in the past year, and no one knows that he is currently living in a beautiful residential area outside Dublin... Yes, it is hard to believe that a revolutionary party member would actually live in a red house outside Dublin.

Four Hundredth Anniversary of the German Painter Burgkmair 194

— Deming

In 1928, the people of Nuremberg, Germany, celebrated the four hundredth anniversary of the birth of their most famous historical figure - the great painter Durer. Three years later (this year), the people of Augsburg celebrated the four hundredth anniversary of the birth of "Augsburg's Durer" -

Hans Burgkmair - The most important of the celebrations was the exhibition of Burgkmair's works.

The small house where Burgkmair lived when he was born still exists. It is located in the most secluded corner of the city. He spent almost all his life there, except for visiting the woodcut master Schongauer in Alsace when he was eighteen and going to Italy several times. Although his trips to Italy were very short, they were extremely important to the progress of his art. Originally, Italy was the center of art at that time. When Mr. Burgkmair was in Italy, he lingered in art galleries every day, looked at famous masterpieces, and gained a lot.

He was the brother-in-law of the portrait painter Holbein the Elder (Holbein father and son were both famous painters, the father was called Holbein the Elder to distinguish him from his son). Durer was his friend and also the person who had the greatest influence on his art.

Burgkmair's works are divided into two categories: (1) Woodcuts - he produced no less than seven hundred woodcuts, all of which are rich in the spirit of freedom. These woodcuts are mostly serial works (Service). The most famous is "The Triumph of Emperor Maximilian I," which consists of one hundred and thirty-five large works, using chiaroscuro to achieve the ultimate in art. (2) Paintings - Paintings are divided into two categories: (1) Portrait paintings and (2) Landscape paintings. In the eyes of many critics, his paintings are his most mature works. His paintings had a great influence on many painters of his time. Originally, he was the first person to introduce the spirit of the Renaissance into German painting. His contribution to German painting is equal to the contribution of Riermenschneider to German sculpture, and his influence is more lasting than Riermenschneider.
